Current Commentary

Research on Japan (II)

Regarding the importance of studying the Japanese question, there are indeed many insightful and incisive arguments from domestic scholars. However, speakers are earnest, and listeners are indifferent. In this regard, Chinese people always feel that it is insignificant. Compared to Japan's research on us, the government advocates from above, and the people work hard from below. Many scholars and experts are doing their best, fearing to fall behind. The difference is truly immeasurable. Mr. Jiang Menglin also made a poignant remark on the attitude of Chinese people towards Japan, saying, "In the past forty years, our country's attitude towards Japan has changed three times. Before the Sino-Japanese War, it was contempt; after the Sino-Japanese War, it was emulation; since the Twenty-One Demands, it has been hatred. Contempt led to the defeat in the Sino-Japanese War. Emulation led to the Reform Movement. Extreme hatred turns back to contempt. In terms of modern academics, Japan is not as good as Europe and the United States. But its ability to absorb the strengths of others and blend them with the customs of its own nation is also a characteristic. How can we despise it? Therefore, we should study Japan deeply. The reason is not only to know ourselves and our enemy. Shortsighted people have not heard of the rapid progress of Japanese academics in recent years, and when they talk about Japan, they often express contempt. It seems not worth studying. Alas, have we forgotten the lesson of the Sino-Japanese War?" These words are poignant and thought-provoking. Japan was established in the islands and was initially a completely bare and uncultured nation. Only after the introduction of our country's culture did it have culture to speak of. This is an undeniable fact. However, after the Meiji Restoration, it worked hard to govern and vigorously reformed, taking the spiritual civilization of the East and the material civilization of the West, merging and integrating them to adapt them to its own life and use. At the same time, its people were united and diligent, working for the country and the nation tirelessly. This kind of upward national spirit has driven its country to become increasingly prosperous. Japan after the Meiji Restoration is no longer the Japan that Ono Imoko, dispatched to our country to import civilization six or seven years ago. Our country, being ignorant of the situation in Japan and treating people as barbarians, was arrogant. In the Sino-Japanese War, Japan, knowing that we were unprepared, was even more prepared. We knew nothing about it. Not to mention its outward development plans, diplomatic policies, and national secrets, we were ignorant of its military preparations at the time. People had already decided to fight, but we still repeatedly called for peace. Our contempt and ignorance of others were such that defeat was inevitable. This is how the country's contempt for Japan led to defeat in the Sino-Japanese War. After the defeat in the Sino-Japanese War, the Chinese people were shocked by the power of a new and emerging nation nearby. Those who had despised it now emulated it. So they sent people to investigate and sent people to study abroad. All of the country's industries and military preparations hired Japanese consultants for guidance. They worked hard to imitate the Japanese, almost taking this as the great way to revitalize the country. This trend led to the Reform Movement during the Qing Dynasty of Guangxu. This cannot be said to be a good phenomenon of emulation. However, they emulated its superficial aspects but ignored its essence. They studied its outer form but ignored its inner secrets. They envied Japan, but they cannot be said to have understood Japan. Moreover, most of the students sent to Japan at that time studied military affairs and crash courses in politics and law. After returning to the country, there were many who could stand out and take it as their own responsibility to save the country. However, there were also many who studied military affairs and crash courses in politics and law and then became warlords and politicians after returning to the country, poisoning our country and society and becoming the main actors in the political turmoil of our country in the past two or three decades. This is the result of emulation. In the fourth year of the Republic, Japan made unreasonable Twenty-One Demands on us. The Chinese people were extremely angry and turned to hatred. They called for national salvation and revenge in unison and appealed to justice and reason, seeking help from the great powers and calling for help from the China Association. However, they never paid attention to how to probe Japanese conspiracies, how to understand Japanese strength, and how to study Japanese weaknesses. Some even became so hostile to Japan that they did not want to see Japanese people, did not want to learn Japanese, and did not want to hear anything about Japanese politics or have any contact with Japan. The more they hated Japan, the deeper the estrangement. Therefore, after the fourth year of the Republic, the Chinese people spoke of resisting Japan every day, but internal conflicts and disasters arose one after another, and Japan's encroachment on and humiliation of us became more and more rampant. This is the result of hatred. In summary, contempt for Japan, emulation of Japan, and hatred of Japan are not enough to defend ourselves or resist insults. The only way to seek self-defense and resist insults is to understand Japan. It goes without saying that diplomats should know Japan. Even the general public in the country, and even young students, should have a considerable amount of common knowledge about Japan. Only by knowing the other person can we defend ourselves. Only then can we thwart the arrogance and ambitions of the Japanese. In recent years, the Japanese have been afraid of the increasing national power of the Soviet Union and have gradually become its powerful neighbor and enemy. In order to prepare in advance, they have studied the Soviet Union, such as organizing academic societies, publishing monthly magazines, and compiling series of books, working tirelessly to understand the other party in order to compete in the future battlefield. Their far-sightedness and deep insights are truly something that should alert our people.

International Telegrams

France and Germany Hold Paris Conference

Both Sides Have Similar Opinions

A Prelude to Cooperation Between the Two Countries

London Governing Council Scheduled to Open Tonight

Limited to Discussing Germany's Economic Woes

German Banks Sign Contracts with Each Other

To Prevent the Occurrence of a Run on Banks

▲ Nationalist Press dispatch from Paris, 18th: German Chancellor Brüning and Foreign Minister Curtius arrived at the Paris station at 2:00 PM today. They were greeted by a large crowd, creating quite a spectacle. To maintain order, the French authorities deployed a large detachment of guards in addition to the police. After Brüning and his party arrived at the station, they were greeted by French Prime Minister Laval, Foreign Minister Briand, and other officials. Brüning and his party then proceeded by car to the German Embassy. Many journalists requested interviews, but Brüning was unable to respond to them all. However, he later issued a statement saying that the German government was very pleased to have this opportunity to discuss various important issues between the two countries with the French government. This conference had been planned for a long time, but its significance is now even more important than before. This conference is not only to clear the clouds between the two countries, but also to discuss and resolve various special problems that affect Germany and other countries. Therefore, it is firmly believed that this conference will achieve satisfactory results. Germany will be able to present its needs to France and gain its understanding, and enhance friendship between Germany and France, and so on.

▲ Nationalist Press dispatch from Paris, 18th: The German-French conference began at 4:30 PM today at the Ministry of Foreign Affairs. In addition to Brüning and Curtius, the German side was also attended by German Ambassador Hoesch, Permanent Secretary of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs Boye, and Counselor of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs Schiffer. The French side was represented by Laval, Briand, Finance Minister Flandin, Budget Minister Piétri, Secretary of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs Berthelot, and Undersecretary of Foreign Affairs Ponsot. After the meeting began, the Prime Minister first presented Germany's financial situation, followed by French Finance Minister Flandin describing France's rescue plans. The two sides then exchanged views based on the above approaches. According to the post-meeting announcement, both sides had very harmonious opinions. The German-French conference ended at 9:00 PM and is scheduled to continue tomorrow afternoon. (Reuters dispatch) Grandi may join the meeting at that time. According to news from Rome, the Italian Foreign Minister has left for London to attend the Governing Council meeting, and will stop in Paris to participate in the talks. After today's meeting, the atmosphere is indeed more optimistic.

▲ Reuters dispatch from Paris, 19th: The interior ministry district is usually quiet every Sunday. This morning at 10:00 a.m., cars carrying more than twenty representatives from the United States, France, Britain, Germany, Japan, and Italy arrived in succession to hold a preliminary meeting before the London Governing Council meeting, which suddenly made the area lively. France insisted that the London conference should be limited to saving the economic disaster and should not involve issues such as disarmament and the Young Plan. After the representatives met at the Ministry of the Interior this morning, they decided that the London Governing Council meeting would focus on studying Germany's finances and

Joint Sports Meet between British and American Universities

The American Team Defeats the British Team

▲ Reuters dispatch from London, 18th: The joint sports team of Harvard and Yale Universities in the United States competed today at Stamford Bridge with the joint sports team of Oxford and Cambridge Universities in Britain. The American team won 7.5 to 4.5 against the British team. The Americans won the half-mile run, 120-yard hurdles, throwing the hammer, one-mile run, 220-yard low hurdles, quarter-mile run, and pole vault. The British team took the lead in the 100-yard dash, 220-yard dash, three-mile run, and long jump. In the high jump, each team got half a point. There have been ten Anglo-American university sports meets in total, and the Americans have now won six times.

Public Telegram

Telegram from the National Products Exhibition Hall of the Ministry of Industry to all newspaper offices, forwarded to all levels of party headquarters, all agencies, and all organizations nationwide for your attention: This time, the Japanese imperialists, under the pretext of the Wanpaoshan Incident, dispatched troops and police in an attempt to create another May 3rd Massacre to realize their aggression. They are still harboring evil intentions, becoming more and more unscrupulous, instigating Koreans to massacre overseas Chinese, abandoning public reason, and violating humanity. All those with blood in their veins are filled with indignation. We, based on our position of promoting national products and supporting revolutionary diplomacy, believe that to fatally subdue the Japanese imperialists, it is not in a moment of excitement, but in permanent perseverance. Therefore, for economic severance of relations, we must first devote ourselves to production. To seek increased production, we must promote national products. Promoting national products is an economic national defense movement, and striving for production is a key plan for national salvation. We hope that compatriots across the country will abide by this intention, act as defenders, and express their grievances. We hope you will take note. The National Products Exhibition Hall of the Ministry of Industry, Capital National Products Movement Basic District Committee, Xiao Yin.

Telegram from Kaifeng

To all newspaper offices for your attention: Henan is unfortunate, with famines occurring frequently for years. Military affairs have just been settled, and natural disasters have struck again. In eastern Henan, such as Luyi; in northern Henan, such as Mengxian and Jiyuan; and in western Henan, such as Dengfeng, Songxian, Yanshi, Lushi, and Mianchi counties, huge hailstones have caused disaster, destroying all crops in the fields, with corpses everywhere, and cries shaking the heavens. We are planning ways to provide relief to save these people from disaster, but in eastern Henan, such as Yancheng, Xihua, Linying, and Xiangcheng; and in southern Henan, such as Dengxian, Zhengyang, Xichuan, Yexian, Xiping, Huangchuan, Xixian, Shangcheng, Xinyang, and Luoshan, there have been torrential rains for weeks, causing floods. The water is raging, bringing wind and rain together, with houses collapsing and being swept away by the waves. Fields and homes are flooded, and people and animals are adrift. Fathers and sons are separated, and husbands and wives are scattered. The dead are buried in the bellies of fish, and the living are crying out with exhaustion. Now, the Huai River is overflowing, and only three versions of the city are left in dozens of towns. The Sha River has burst its banks, and there is a lack of grain harvest in hundreds of miles. Some people are trapped in the mud and cannot reach the shore, and others cling to the treetops, hoping for rescue but no boat arrives. It is pitiful that they are saved today, but their homes are destroyed. How can they plan for clothing and food when they are out of danger in the future? This is truly an unprecedented disaster and extreme pain in this moment. Fang is in charge of civil administration and dares not embrace peace. My heart is apprehensive and deeply worried. Now, I sincerely call for help and shed tears to seek assistance. I hope that compatriots who are sinking and dying will embody the virtues of heaven and earth, deliver relief grain early, universally save the people from disaster, generously donate money, and jointly achieve good deeds. The telegram is filled with urgency and panic. Zhang Fang kowtows.

Special Article

Red Peril and China's Survival (Continued)

Yang Xingfo

The Red Army's organization takes the pseudo-Chinese Soviet Republic's Central Revolutionary Military Commission as its highest command organ. Under the Military Commission, there are two offices, the Yangtze Military Commission and the Southern Military Commission, as well as six regional military commissions in Hubei-Henan-Anhui, Hunan-Hubei border, Jiangxi-Northeast, Guangxi Right River, Fujian-Guangdong-Jiangxi, and Hainan Island. The actual strength of its troops varies greatly according to various investigations. According to the investigation in the autumn of last year, there were a total of fourteen armies, with about 70,000 soldiers and about 50,000 rifles. According to Gao Zhanjun's estimate in the "Overview of the Communist Disaster in Jiangxi" in March of this year, the Red Army has at least 80,000 guns and 200,000 people (see the Semi-Monthly Communist Production Journal). According to the "Current Work Plan for the Soviet Region" seized this spring, it has been reorganized into seven armies.

Under the seven armies, there are a total of sixteen divisions and five independent regiments. In addition, there are two guard divisions directly under the command and the Qiongya Independent Division, totaling nineteen divisions and five independent regiments (based on Minister He Yingqin's report to the National Assembly on the inside story of the Red Bandits in Jiangxi). In addition to the guns obtained and the number of people increased this year due to the defeats of the government army, the recent Red Army soldiers are estimated to be around 300,000, with about 120,000 guns. Although the Communist Party claims to take the Workers' and Peasants' Red Army as the backbone force in the Communist Party's war, in the "Current Work Plan for the Soviet Region," regarding the composition of the Red Army, it is said that "the composition of the Red Army is mostly not composed of hired peasants, poor peasants, and coolies as the basic troops. Even the most powerful Fourth and Fifth Armies are still composed of soldiers as the backbone, and the workers' armies are more composed of bandits and hooligans. Most of the main cadres of the Red Army are not workers." Therefore, the so-called Workers' and Peasants' Red Army is only an ideal term. The political commissar of each army is the backbone of an army and has the power to supervise military commanders, which is the Soviet system of the party governing the army. In addition to the Red Army, there is also the Red Guard. All men and women in the bandit area between the ages of eighteen and forty-five who do not exploit the labor of others are obliged to serve as Red Guards. Those in towns are the Red Police Guards, divided into standing and reserve types. The standing teams are separated from production and are solely responsible for defending the locality. The reserve teams are not separated from production, but must receive regular armed training. Those in the countryside are the peasant Red Guards, who are not separated from production, but their organization and training are all prepared to be mobilized at any time. The spear teams are part of the Red Guards. Between the Red Army and the Red Guards, there are guerrillas as the Red Army's reserve army. In addition, there are children's teams, or labor children's groups, organized by children aged ten to fifteen, who are responsible for inspecting pedestrians. There are Young Pioneers, organized by young people aged sixteen to eighteen. The task of killing and charging is often assigned to the Young Pioneers. Regarding military education, it is heard that in Jiangxi, there are Red Army cadre schools and military political schools. Women participate in the Red Guards and various social organizations and have the same status as men, with no independent organization. However, the so-called comfort teams and laundry teams are exclusively for women. Young and middle-aged women mostly serve as comfort team members, and older women serve as laundry team members.

Due to the scarcity of guns and bullets, the Red Army often uses cunning tactics in combat: (1) Enticement and encirclement, luring the National Army to mountainous and densely forested areas in the red area for ambushes. (2) Feint to the east and attack the west, pretending to attack a certain place, first going in the other direction, then suddenly turning back to attack the National Army with lightning speed. (3) Avoid the strong and attack the weak, dispersing to avoid strong enemies, and concentrating to encircle weak enemies. (4) Utilizing the masses, using workers and peasants to plant red flags and blow trumpets in the mountains to disrupt the National Army, or using workers and peasants as vanguards to exhaust the National Army's bullets, and then the Red Army would unite to attack fiercely when the National Army was tired. (5) Preserving strength, the Red Army does not engage in attacking fortified positions, does not fight hard battles, does not fight without knowing the enemy's situation, and does not easily fight in areas without Communist Party and bandit-influenced masses. All this is because bullets are too few and difficult to replenish, so they are unwilling to take risks lightly. (6) Shaking the enemy's morale, the Red Army often sends workers, peasants, and women to the National Army to make strong propaganda to shake the morale of the army. The above-mentioned tactics have been tried repeatedly and are mostly familiar to the National Army, so their effectiveness has been greatly reduced.

The Communist Party's program and mass organizations. Because the Communist Party wants to gain the support of poor peasants to consolidate its regime in the Soviet area, it calls for the thorough implementation of land revolution. Its current ten major programs are: (1) Overthrow imperialist rule; (2) Confiscate the enterprises and banks of foreign capitalists; (3) Unify China and recognize the right to national self-determination; (4) Overthrow the Nationalist government; (5) Establish a government of workers, peasants, and soldiers' representatives (Soviets); (6) Implement an eight-hour working day, increase wages, unemployment relief, and social insurance; (7) Confiscate all the land of the landlord class and return the cultivated land to the peasants; (8) Improve the lives of soldiers and give soldiers land and work; (9) Abolish all taxes from government warlords and local areas and implement a unified progressive tax; (10) Unite the world's proletariat and unite Soviet Russia. Among these ten major programs, only the seventh article, confiscating the land of the landlord class, has indeed been realized. However, what they are doing is a temporary distribution of land, not a real land revolution under communism. The ninth article, abolishing taxes, only abolishes the taxes of the original government offices and replaces them with their new taxes, such as the progressive land tax and the wood and public welfare fees. It is not enough to replace them with fines (specifying local tyrants, landlords, and rich peasants; those who can be fined more than eighty yuan must be fined) and grain collection (when new grains are first harvested, each household is required to keep a certain amount of grain per person per year, and the rest is registered in a book, and when necessary, the grain committee can take it away at any time) and other methods to raise funds and sufficient food.

Regarding the land revolution, there is also the Chinese Communist Party's eight major programs for the land revolution in 1930, the content of which is: (1) Overthrow the power of local tyrants, landlords, and bureaucratic authorities, disarm the counter-revolutionary forces, disarm the peasants, and establish the power of peasant conferences in rural areas; (2) Confiscate the property and land of the landlord class immediately without compensation. The confiscated land will be handled by the peasant conference and distributed to landless and land-poor peasants for use; (3) The properties of ancestral halls, temples, churches, and other public properties, official wastelands, or ownerless wastelands and sand fields will be handled by the peasant representative conference (Soviet) and distributed to peasants for use; (4) Each province and region will have a portion of land for the (Soviet) government to use for immigration and reclamation and to be distributed to workers, peasants, and soldiers for economic use; (5) Announce that all high-interest loan agreements are invalid; (6) Burn all land deeds of local tyrant governments and other contracts that exploit peasants, including written and oral agreements; (7) Abolish all taxes promulgated by warlords and local government offices, abolish the system of contract taxes and likin, and establish a single progressive agricultural economic tax; (8) The state will help the agricultural economy: A. Undertake land projects; B. Improve and expand water conservancy; C. Prevent natural disasters; D. The state will handle immigration affairs; E. The state will operate agricultural banks and credit cooperatives to handle low-interest loans; F. Unify the currency and unify weights and measures; G. All rivers will be managed and operated by the Soviet government.

Among these eight major programs, those that have been implemented are the confiscation of property and land and the destruction of deeds and the distribution of land. The land distribution procedures are as follows: (1) All public land, temple land, ancestral hall land, and land of large landlords (including semi-landlords, rich peasants, and rented land) will be completely confiscated without conditions. All land deeds and official documents will be burned, and the ridges of the fields will be leveled to completely eliminate the boundaries and evidence of the original landlords. (2) The land in each township will be executed and equally distributed by the township's workers', peasants', and soldiers' conference (Soviet). (3) Distribution will be based on population and labor, and all male and female citizens with the ability to work will have the right to distribute land. (4) Citizens without the ability to work (children under the age of sixteen and the elderly and disabled) will be supported by their families or lodging families, and citizens whose burdens are increased as a result will be given additional land as appropriate. (5) The number of acres to be distributed to each person in each township and the number of additional acres to be added due to increased burdens will be determined by the local Soviet in accordance with local conditions, but the number of additional acres per person cannot exceed one-fourth of the number of acres to be distributed (according to this restriction, the elderly, disabled, and underage children will be effectively reduced their right to survival, and the Soviet has no remedy for this, because these people are of no use to the Red Army, so they do not hesitate to sacrifice them). (6) When the population of one place is too large and there is not enough land to be distributed, a portion of the people can be moved to a neighboring place with fewer people. (7) Families of Red Army soldiers, under the condition that no one can farm, the local Soviet can find someone to farm on their behalf (this is the method of the Communist Party to lure soldiers. The former landlord is now a Red Army soldier, and the former tenant farmer is now a tenant farmer for the Red Army, so the Red Army is actually a new landlord class). (To be continued)

Important News

Commander-in-Chief Chiang Returns to Nanchang from the Front Line

▲ Brief Overview of the Itinerary After Leaving Nanchang on the 2nd

▲ After Recapturing Guangchang, He Orders His Car Back to the Province

Nanchang Correspondence: Commander-in-Chief Chiang departed for the front line on the 2nd of this month. On the 3rd, he arrived safely in Fuzhou and stayed at the forward headquarters of the Eighth Middle School, where he discussed the left-wing operation plan with He Yingqin and gave instructions. On the 5th, he departed for Nancheng. At that time, the Red Bandits focused on southeastern Jiangxi and the Fujian border, planning to attack Nanfeng and Nancheng with all their strength in order to get out of Fujian and Zhejiang. Therefore, Chiang urgently needed to go there in person to encourage morale. After arriving in Nancheng on the 6th, he summoned the generals and gave instructions. Afterwards, he also went to Lichuan and Nanfeng to inspect and command. However, only senior generals knew about it. On the 11th, he supervised the troops and recaptured Kangdu, a key point on the Fujian border. Then he advanced and captured Guangchang. The main force of the Red Bandits had been scattered. However, Chiang felt that the front line was winning victories, and important matters in the headquarters and the central government needed to be handled urgently. Therefore, on the morning of the 16th, he took a civilian boat from Nancheng back to the province. That night, he arrived in Fuzhou and met with He Yingqin for an hour. He then took a civilian boat downstream. At dawn on the 17th, he arrived at Xiebu, which is about forty or fifty miles from the province (some say Yangjiadu, some say Wanshe). He then went ashore and walked to Liantang Station on the Nan-Zhang Road. He Yaozu, Lu Dipin, and Xiong Shihui, who were in Qingyunpu at the time, received the news and rushed to Liantang to greet him. They then took the same car to Qingyunpu to attend the public funeral of the late Division Commander Hu. At that time, Chiang was wearing a straw hat, a light gray straight silk robe, and black leather shoes. His face was slightly darker than before. At around 9:00 AM, the public funeral ceremony of Division Commander Hu was held, presided over by Chiang. After the ceremony, Chiang and Xiong, He, Lu, and others took separate cars back to the province. Military police were densely deployed from Zhongshan Road in the provincial capital to the station. At around 10:00 AM, Chiang arrived at the headquarters. All the important figures in the province went to pay their respects and report everything. As to whether Chiang will go to the front again, nothing is known yet. (July 17th)

Second Batch of Refugees Arrives in Qingdao

▲ Li Zhonggang Also Arrives in Qingdao to Report to Beijing

Qingdao Correspondence: The first batch of refugees escaping from Korea arrived in Qingdao on the 15th by the Kyodo Maru from Yantai, totaling 807 people. 165 people were transported to Shijiusuo by the Gyeongheung and Yuseong on the 15th. 574 people took the Taesung merchant ship to Shijiusuo on the 16th to return to their hometowns. The above-mentioned merchant ships were all assigned by the Shipping Association and fulfilled their obligations. The remaining 68 people were all residents along the Jiaoji Railway line. After consultation between the Social Affairs Bureau, the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, and the Railway Bureau, a carriage was attached to the 11th train at 3:00 PM on the 16th to transport them back to their hometowns. The Social Affairs Bureau also sent personnel to escort the train to take care of them. The second batch of refugees arrived in Qingdao this morning (17th) at 12:00 PM by the Changping Maru and the Gyeonggi Maru, totaling 798 people. The Gyeonggi Maru sailed from Incheon to Qingdao, carrying 357 refugees. These refugees had some property, so after landing, most of them found inns to live in on their own. At noon, they elected dozens of representatives to go to the Municipal Steering Committee to describe the plight of the refugees and said that this riot by Koreans was guided by Japanese police, so the Koreans were fearless and their cruel methods were even worse than the Red Bandits. They were crying while speaking. It was found that most of these refugees were from Shouguang and Changle. Tonight or tomorrow morning, they will take the Jiaoji Railway train back to their original hometowns. The Changping Maru came from Yantai, carrying 441 refugees, all of whom lived by farming or doing hard labor in Korea. Women and children accounted for half of them. They were supporting the old and carrying the young, which was very pitiful. After landing, they were led by members of the Municipal Chamber of Commerce and temporarily accommodated in the New Stage. They were also provided with steamed buns, pot cakes, and boiled water for the refugees to eat. Representatives from all walks of life went to express their condolences, one after another. It is heard that the Shipping Association has assigned three merchant ships to transport more than 200 people to Shijiusuo for landing at 6:00 PM today, so that they can return to their hometowns. Another carriage was borrowed from the Jiaoji Railway and attached to the first train tonight to send about 70 people scattered along the Jiaoji Railway line back to their hometowns. The rest will temporarily stay in the New Stage and be transported tomorrow when there are ships available. It is heard that there will be a third batch of refugees arriving in Qingdao tomorrow. In addition, Li Zhonggang, the head of the Consulate General in Korea, also came to Qingdao on the Gyeonggi Maru on the same day. Li also brought a report detailing the beginning and end of the Korean riot. It is heard that Li will take a ship to Shanghai and then to Beijing to report everything to the central government. (July 17th)

Refugees Arrive in Jinan via Yantai

▲ A Total of Forty-One People

Jinan Correspondence: After the case of Koreans massacring our overseas Chinese occurred, the overseas Chinese in Korea fled back to China one after another. Everywhere they passed, they were entertained by various chambers of commerce. At 3:19 PM today (17th), refugees from Incheon, Zhao Xushan, Liu Zhenbiao, and others, and refugees from Pyongyang, Liu Jingyuan, Li Jingshen, and others, arrived in Jinan by the 13th train of the Jiaoji Railway. Most of them looked like workers and were in a state of desperation. After getting off the train, they were treated to lunch by the Relief Association and then sent to the Henan Guild Hall on Guanyi Street by the Public Security Bureau's Second Branch, where everything was taken care of by the Xixiang Branch. According to refugees from Incheon, they boarded a ship on the 7th and went to Yantai, and arrived in Weixian by car on the 11th. They boarded the train from Wei early today (17th). According to refugees from Pyongyang, they boarded a ship from Nampo on the 11th, passed through Yantai, and transferred to Qingdao, arriving in Jinan today. This time, Koreans massacred overseas Chinese after the Japanese gave them a five-day deadline to kill at will. Koreans marched in flag-waving formations, blowing horns and drums. Some used bamboo poles more than ten feet long, sharpened into spears, some held sticks, some held stones, and some had large carts in the back, loaded with large quantities of stones to use as weapons. The clothing, money, and furniture of the overseas Chinese were looted by Koreans, and the rest were destroyed. The Japanese, although stating that they would protect our overseas Chinese after the incident, secretly helped the Koreans. The overseas Chinese, believing that the Japanese were protecting them, would not be in danger again, so they took off their clothes and went to bed peacefully. Unexpectedly, they fell into the Japanese trap. At night, Koreans broke into houses and massacred almost all the Chinese. In Incheon and Pyongyang alone, no more than one or two percent of the overseas Chinese managed to escape alive. The reason why we were able to escape alive was thanks to the green gauze tents, which served as a guarantee. The Japanese still used their cunning tricks, destroying their houses and injuring their horses, claiming to the overseas Chinese that the Korean riots had nothing to do with Japan, etc., making false efforts and it is regrettable. It was also found that the refugees who came to Jinan this time had been in Korea for eight or nine years, and some for one or two years. Their jobs included working in factories, farming, and doing business. Most of them were from Jining, Boping, Changqing, and other counties. This time, there were 24 people from Incheon, 17 people from Pyongyang, a total of 41 people, including four women and seven children. (17th)

Documents Regarding the Wanbaoshan Incident Negotiations Between China and Japan (5)

▲Letter from the Municipal Affairs Office to the Japanese Consul: Respectfully, regarding the case of Korean people at Wanbaoshan forcefully excavating civilian land to dig waterways and compelling the diversion of the Yitong River, multiple letters have been received previously, stating that investigations were being carried out and the resolution plan agreed upon on June 8th was being implemented, with the withdrawal of police and cessation of work. The issue of the remaining Korean people's departure or stay, and the matter of damage compensation between the parties involved, were previously discussed in our letter to your office on June 17th for your opinion, so as to resolve them as soon as possible. However, today we received an official document from the Changchun County Government, stating that on the 17th of this month, Wang Zhongfu, Meng Xiansi, and Jiang Yuanting from Guanhuangtun reported that their farmland was about seven or eight li from the Yitong River. Recently, continuous rain has caused mountain water to flow down, but the existing ditch was blocked by Korean residents, preventing the water from flowing downstream. Their farmland is currently flooded, and if the original state is not restored promptly, the damage in the future will be immeasurable. Furthermore, the Third Branch Bureau reported that about one li west of Jiangjiawobao Village, there are 73 Korean people and 2 Japanese police officers still digging ditches and surveying for the construction of a reservoir, planning to sow seeds in about one or two days. We are requested to negotiate and stop them from proceeding. Upon investigation, the aforementioned water diversion project, as a result of a joint investigation by both parties, indeed infringes upon the landowners' rights and is significantly harmful to the nearby farmland. This project violates the purpose of the agreement reached by both parties on June 8th to resolve this case in a fair and optimal manner after investigation. Naturally, it cannot continue. The original state should be restored swiftly to appease the farmers' earnest hope. According to the reported situation, if your side does not immediately stop them, all resulting complications and consequences will be your responsibility, as stated in our letter of June 12th. This letter is hereby sent for your attention. We urge you to faithfully implement the previous agreement and promptly respond to our original letter regarding resolving the remaining issues of this case, so as to bring it to a conclusion. Respectfully addressed to Mr. Tashiro, Japanese Consul stationed in Changchun, June 23rd.

▲Letter from the Japanese Consulate to the Municipal Affairs Office: Respectfully, regarding the issue of Korean people cultivating paddy fields at Wanbaoshan, we have previously conducted a joint investigation with your office. However, due to differing opinions on the outcome, negotiations have remained stalled, which is truly regrettable. Subsequently, on the 24th of this month, we had another face-to-face discussion. Although I expressed my sincere views at that time, there was ultimately no hope of reaching a completely unified agreement. However, the Korean side is quite anxious as the sowing season has passed. If I were to order them to stop the damming construction, this year's paddy field cultivation

Page 8

would be equivalent to abandoning it, making it difficult to stop. Therefore, while continuing negotiations, I still hope for a satisfactory resolution. However, to accommodate the wishes of the Korean people, they should be allowed to implement the damming and sowing to see what the outcome will be and whether the water damage is as serious as the opposing farmers fear. This is a last resort for me in my position. I sincerely hope that our two sides will work together to take the best measures to prevent unfortunate events. Otherwise, in the event that unfortunate events occur due to negligence in prevention, a thorough investigation should be conducted to clarify responsibility. The above situation was already discussed in person on the 24th, and this letter is sent for your attention. Respectfully addressed to Zhou, Director of the Changchun Municipal Preparatory Office, Tashiro Shigenori, Consul stationed in Changchun, June 26th.

▲Letter from the Japanese Consul to the Municipal Affairs Office: Respectfully, according to a report, on the afternoon of the 24th, at 8 PM, two Korean people were walking near Mashao Kou when they encountered 14 patrol police officers from the Second District Public Security Bureau, who tied them up with ropes, beat them, robbed them of the millet and gold they were carrying, and then protected the local farmers from the side, destroying about 18 zhang of the excavated waterway and repeatedly firing shots to threaten the Korean people. Afterward, they left with the farmers, heading west. The official authorities of your country have absolutely no intention of rejecting the Korean people, as your director has repeatedly stated. Now that the aforementioned incident has occurred, it is difficult for us to continue to trust your officials, and it may lead to a situation where we have no choice but to directly protect the Korean people. I sincerely hope that such acts of violence by your officials will not occur again in the future and that you will seek appropriate measures. The above situation was already conveyed in person by a staff member on the 25th, and this letter is sent for your attention. Respectfully addressed to Zhou, Director of the Changchun Municipal Preparatory Office, Tashiro Shigenori, Consul stationed in Changchun, June 26th.

▲Letter from the Municipal Affairs Office to the Japanese Consul: Respectfully, your official document No. 47 of June 26th has been received. Regarding the case of Koreans at Wanbaoshan forcefully excavating civilian land to dig waterways, intending to build a dam across the river to forcibly divert the river for irrigation, a joint on-site investigation by both parties revealed that not only would the completion of the dam cause enormous damage to the farmland along the river, but also the right of ownership of the land through which the waterway passes is being infringed upon. More than 40 households of farmland are cut into two sections, causing inconvenience for each household's cultivation, and resulting in permanent and unlimited losses. Furthermore, navigation and transportation between Changchun and Nong'an counties will also be interrupted due to the completion of the dam. All of this is not permitted by current laws and regulations, and any country or any nation would not allow such unreasonable actions. The actual situation after the aforementioned joint investigation was formally communicated in our letter of June 11th. If your consul orders the Korean people to continue the aforementioned illegal acts, infringing upon the landowners and farmers' legitimate and inherent rights, your side should bear full responsibility for all disputes and losses that may arise in the future, as formally communicated in our letter of June 12th, with a solemn statement. Based on the aforementioned reasons, it is expected that you have noted our response. Respectfully addressed to Mr. Tashiro, Japanese Consul stationed in Changchun, June 27th.

▲Letter from the Municipal Affairs Office to the Japanese Consul: Respectfully, your official document No. 48 of June 26th has been read. Regarding the section of the Wanbaoshan waterway that was filled in for about 18 zhang on the afternoon of the 24th, our investigation revealed that it was indeed the farmers in that area who took advantage of their free time to selectively fill in the waterway dug by the Korean people on their farmland, which caused much inconvenience for their cultivation and travel, to restore it to its original state for ease of passage and to avoid hindering farming operations. The claim in your letter that 14 police officers were present to protect them is, according to the Changchun County Government's investigation, completely unfounded. Based on the aforementioned reasons, this response is sent for your attention. Respectfully addressed to Mr. Tashiro, Japanese Consul stationed in Changchun, June 27th.

All Chinese people have been gnashing their teeth at this, and this time's act of using a knife to kill is particularly insidious. We earnestly request your ministry and government to raise a serious negotiation with Japan in order to save the lives of overseas Chinese and maintain national rights. The electric message cannot express the extreme indignation. Sincerely, the Congress of Representatives of All Circles in Hankou. The telegram to the country was similar and is omitted. (July 18th)

Hooliganism Case by the Japanese Garrison in Huanggu Tun

Shenyang Dispatch: It is common practice for Japanese military and police to stab Chinese people in various parts of the Northeast, and it is not surprising. At about 4 PM on the 14th of this month, another incident occurred near the San Dong Bridge on the South Manchurian Railway in Huanggu Tun, where Japanese garrison troops recklessly attacked Chinese pedestrians, causing a dispute, which led to the dispatch of a large number of armed Japanese police to surround the police station in charge. The details are as follows: A few steps from the scene of the incident, on the left side of the San Kong Bridge on the South Manchurian Railway, is the San Dong Bridge Police Station, which is under the jurisdiction of the Second Branch Bureau of the Commercial Port. The South Manchurian Railway track is on the bridge, and there is a Japanese soldier's post. Normally, from their high vantage point, they randomly throw stones at Chinese pedestrians, often causing head injuries and bloodshed, leaving people helpless. Therefore, people generally regard the bridge arch as a "tiger's mouth," and they would never dare to pass through it rashly unless absolutely necessary. At 4:10 PM on the afternoon of that day, two Chinese men, Shen Yuhuai and Wu Xizhen, both from Hebei Province, who made a living as rickshaw pullers, went to Xita to visit friends. On their way back, when they approached the San Dong Bridge, they suddenly saw a Japanese garrison soldier, fully armed, carrying a large rifle, marching proudly forward. Thinking that the Japanese soldier was following closely behind them, and fearing that he might be drunk or looking for trouble, they walked to the side to make way in order to avoid a conflict. As the two rickshaw pullers were walking, they were discussing private matters, talking as they walked. Then, Shen looked back and saw that the Japanese soldier was still following behind them, acting suspiciously. So he whispered to Wu Xizhen, "Let's walk to the side, the Japanese soldier is coming." Wu immediately moved to the sidewalk on the side of the road. Unexpectedly, the Japanese soldier deliberately provoked a fight, catching up and shouting, "What are you doing?" After this barely comprehensible Chinese phrase, he immediately raised his gun and struck Shen Yuhuai on the head, breaking a hole above Shen's left eyebrow, causing his eyeball to bulge out, and blood to flow profusely. The two rickshaw pullers were strong and powerful, so they joined forces to hold the perpetrator and dragged him to the San Dong Bridge Police Station to reason with him. While they were wrestling with each other, officer Li Jingkui and guard Ren Yuxiu, who were resting, caught sight of them. They went forward to inquire about the cause of the matter and then went to the police station together. After questioning by station chief Tan Shangwu, the Japanese soldier was first asked his name and unit number, but he did not answer. When asked why he hit someone, he also did not answer, pretending not to understand Chinese. He roared and shouted inside the police station, and even tried to rush out. The police, because he was caught in the act of assaulting someone, could not let him go. They gathered both parties in a room while telephoning Director Hu of the Second Branch Bureau in charge to ask for instructions. After receiving the report, the bureau urgently telegraphed the General Bureau and the Office of the Diplomatic Commissioner to send a translator to the scene for questioning. This was delayed for half an hour. At this time, the Japanese police patrolling the bridge had already reported to the Japanese garrison via telephone. After the report, they also gathered about three nearby Japanese soldiers and went to the police station to demand the release of the man, using rude language and threatening to use force. The situation was extremely urgent, but our negotiators were delayed. At 4:50 PM, the Japanese garrison had already dispatched a large team, including more than one hundred soldiers, more than fifty cavalrymen, and more than fifty armed policemen. The military and police officers traveled in more than ten pedal cars in front, followed by infantry and cavalry, in a threatening manner, as if facing a major enemy. After arriving at the police station, they immediately surrounded it on all sides, set up checkpoints along the way, and cut off traffic. In the end, with their superior numbers and power, our police had no choice but to let them do what they wanted. As a result, they kidnapped the Japanese soldier who caused the trouble and the two Chinese men. After the Japanese soldier who caused the trouble left the police station, he was briefly interrogated by a Japanese officer in a lookout on the side of the railroad (the building had two rooms with a telephone and radio for the Japanese soldiers on the railroad to take shelter from the wind and rain). Then he was released. The kidnapped Shen and Wu were also taken to the building and beaten with whips, wooden sticks, and iron rods without asking the reason, causing serious injuries. At about 5 PM, our negotiators finally arrived, and Director Hu, Section Chief Lin, and Section Chief Han of the Second Branch Bureau went to the lookout to negotiate with the Japanese side. First, they requested the withdrawal of the surrounding military and police. The Japanese side then ordered the police and soldiers to return to their units. Our side then demanded the return of the kidnapped Chinese, but they were already on their last breath. After four hours of negotiations, at about 9 PM, the Japanese side finally agreed to make concessions, sending the injured Chinese to the Japanese Army Hospital for treatment. The medical expenses were to be borne by the Japanese side, and they apologized to our side, resolving to punish the Japanese soldiers who caused the trouble, and guaranteed that the same incident would not happen again in the future. At 12 PM on the 15th, the San Dong Bridge police and the Japanese garrison met under the bridge to show that they were as friendly as before. A case of hooliganism was thus concluded. (July 15th)

Business Tax Rate in Jiangsu Province Remains Unchanged

▲Temporarily Handled in Accordance with the Revised Regulations of the Ministry of Finance

▲New Tax Law to be Implemented Starting in the Twenty-First Year

Xu Baoying, a member of the Jiangsu Provincial Government and Director of the Department of Finance, previously proposed to the Provincial Government Committee that the business tax rate in this province should be temporarily handled in accordance with the revised regulations of the Ministry of Finance, and that the new tax law should be implemented when business licenses are renewed in the twenty-first year after a trial period of three quarters. The Provincial Government Committee has resolved to approve the proposal. His submission stated: In accordance with the instructions of the Supreme Government, the order of the Executive Yuan, and the order of the National Government, a copy of the Business Tax Law is forwarded, and the Department is instructed to instruct all counties and bureaus to comply with it, etc. In accordance with this, compliance is required. However, an examination of the standard for taxation in the Business Tax Law shows that it is specified as three types: (A) Those who use the total business income as the standard, pay a tax rate of 2/1000 to 10/1000; (B) Those who use the business capital as the standard, pay a tax rate of 4/1000 to 10/1000; (C) Those who use the net business income as the standard, pay a tax rate of 2% to 10%. The previous revision of the Jiangsu Province Business Tax Collection Regulations by the Ministry of Finance stipulated two standards: (1) Those who use the business volume as the standard, the tax rate is from 1/1000 to 10/1000; (2) Those who use the capital amount as the standard, the tax rate is from 2/1000 to 20/1000. Comparing the three standards set by the Legislative Yuan with the two standards set by the Ministry of Finance, it is found that there is an additional net income standard, which was not included in the original regulations. Furthermore, the tax rate set by the Legislative Yuan starts at 2/1000 for business volume and 4/1000 for capital amount, which is different from the original tax rate set by the Ministry of Finance. In addition, the net income rate is set at 2% to 10%, which was not included in the original tax rate. After the promulgation of this new tax law, the original text should be followed, and the provincial government should revise the rate according to the business situation. However, upon investigation, disputes in various counties have only just been resolved since the initial collection of business tax in Jiangsu Province, and it is not appropriate to make further changes. It is proposed that the business tax rate for this year's collection be temporarily handled in accordance with the revised regulations of the Ministry of Finance to avoid further disputes. After a trial period of three quarters, and after the business situation has been investigated and there is some clarity, the new tax law will be implemented starting in the twenty-first year when business licenses are renewed. Is this appropriate? This bill is submitted for public decision.
