After the Cancellation of the Fujian Anti-Smoking Investigation Office

▲All Circles Request Punishment for Yuan Jin and Ma Deji

Fuzhou Dispatch: The situation of opposing the Anti-Smoking Investigation Office in various circles of Fujian is extremely enthusiastic. The office has now received an order from the Central Anti-Smoking Committee to be abolished. The Provincial Government has also instructed the Provincial Anti-Smoking Committee that the province's anti-smoking efforts will still be the responsibility of the committee and should not be relaxed in the slightest. The Anti-Smoking Association has been investigating those who were previously involved in fundraising, sending them to the Public Security Bureau for punishment. At the same time, the Fuzhou Addiction Treatment Society has also initiated a civil anti-smoking campaign, requesting the Fire Brigade Federation to notify each shop's fire brigade to find out the brand names and addresses of opium dens, and notify landlords to move them out within a time limit. If they fail to do so, the district police station will be notified to arrest them and seal them. If a tenant is found selling opium in the future, the landlord will be jointly liable. Furthermore, the All Circles Anti-Smoking Support Association stated that Yuan Jin, while serving as the Director of the Mawei Shipyard, plotted to establish an Anti-Smoking Investigation Office, and Ma Deji, the former Director of the Shanghai Shipyard, also ran around and smoothed things over on his behalf. This was destroying the anti-smoking effort and tarnishing the reputation of the navy. A telegram was sent to the Ministry of the Navy requesting punishment. The original telegram is recorded below: To the Ministry of the Navy in Nanjing: Recently, Yuan Jin went to Fujian to open an Anti-Smoking Investigation Office, publicly selling opium, and also instigated his henchman Ma Deji to make arrangements everywhere, hoping to profit from it. He does not comply with the government's orders and does not care about public opinion. He is insane. Yuan Jin, etc., are subordinates of your ministry and are engaged in this harmful opium business, which is an affront to the public. It is requested that he be transferred back and severely punished to serve as a warning and to maintain the reputation of your ministry and protect the glorious history of anti-smoking in our province. We earnestly hope. (July 16th)

Local Communications

Nanhui

The Key Criminal in the Pan Shutang Theft Case is Brought to Shanghai for Trial: Yesterday, detectives from the Shanghai Municipal Public Security Bureau came to the county to bring in the three key criminals Liu Zhengguo, Ye Wenbu, and Lu Hairong in the Pan Shutang theft case to Shanghai for trial. The County Government brought in the criminals and handed them over to the detectives to take away.

Investigation of the Stealing of Accumulated Grain by Boatmen: The County Warehouse Management Committee recently hired Gao Abing, who is in the shipping business, to transport 300 shi of accumulated pre-procured grain to Wuxi. It has been loaded and unloaded three times. Unexpectedly, Gao Abing secretly unloaded the grain in transit, or hid it in the bow and stern of the boat. He swallowed about 40 shi of it. Yesterday, someone reported this to the committee, and it is currently being investigated strictly and secretly.

Songjiang

The Arrest and Interrogation of the Fake Leader Zhang Siquan: Zhang Siquan, the fake leader of the Tai Bao A Shu of Lake Bandits, nicknamed Gaojiao Pai Siquan, after the ringleader Tai Bao A Shu was executed, heard that he had fled into Taihu with his bandit gang. However, the authorities are making great efforts to arrest him and bring him to justice in order to eliminate the root cause. It is now known that Fan Guozhong, the first captain of the first district of the Aquatic Provincial Public Security Team, has arrested the fake leader in a certain place in Wuxi. It is heard that he will be brought to Songjiang soon.

Suzhou

Huang Huiru Suddenly Appears: It is rumored that Huang Huiru, the protagonist of the Huang-Lu love affair, took a train to Shanghai at the Suzhou Railway Station. It is said that at 3:00 PM on the (18th), Huiru, wearing a white floral gauze qipao, jade-colored silk stockings, and satin shoes, went to the railway station with an old woman in her fifties to buy second-class train tickets to Shanghai. When someone who recognized Huang said that it was Huang Huiru, many people watched. Later, the woman went to the women's waiting room, and when someone asked her surname, she replied that her surname was Huang. The receptionist in the women's waiting room also recognized Huang, and the ticket clerk also saw that it was indeed Huang Huiru. Some people said that Huang originally lived in Jianjinqiao Lane in Suzhou, and some people said that Huang would have to come to Suzhou after going to Shanghai. The reporter of this newspaper obtained this information from rumors after the event, and the truth is impossible to judge. In short, this bizarre news has spread throughout Suzhou.

Wuxi

Verdict on the Bloodshed Case at Beizhakou: Zeng Haishan, a resident of Beizhakou, was severely wounded in the head by thugs last winter, narrowly escaping death. Subsequently, Zeng’s concubine, Yao, and her paramour, Sun Kuntao, were arrested and imprisoned on suspicion of murder. Yesterday was the date for the verdict in the case. Presiding Judge Liang ordered Sun Kuntao and Zeng Yao, who were in custody, to be brought to court. After a brief interrogation, the judgment was announced. Sun Kuntao and Zeng Yao were each sentenced to eighteen years of imprisonment for attempted murder and conspiracy to commit murder. After the sentencing, they were sent to prison. However, it is reported that Sun and Zeng were dissatisfied with the verdict and intend to hire a lawyer to draft an appeal to the High Court.

Robbery Occurs at Lengdu Bridge: In the Lengdu Bridge area, District Two (Jingyun City), Village Chief Miao Shunjin, a farmer by profession, lives in modest comfort. He has one son and two daughters. The eldest daughter, aged nineteen, was recently betrothed to a certain family through her uncle's matchmaking. The engagement ceremony was scheduled for the fifteenth of this month. The groom's family had sent forty yuan in cash and gold engagement tokens, totaling over two hundred yuan, which attracted the attention of bandits. Around one in the morning the day before yesterday, five or six bandits suddenly arrived, armed with pistols, and broke into the house. They demanded silence and ransacked the place, rummaging through boxes and chests. After half an hour, they left, each carrying stolen goods. Upon inspection, the losses were estimated at over three hundred yuan. Village Chief Miao, fearing retaliation from the bandits, was reluctant to report the incident to the authorities. It is reported that residents in the area have been robbed four or five times before, but the losses were minor. During the robbery at the Miao residence, the bandits loudly called out, "Is Village Chief Miao at home?" This suggests that the bandits were familiar with the area. If the public security authorities conduct a thorough investigation, it should not be difficult to solve the case soon.

Water Pumping Boat Collapses Huadu Bridge: A water pumping boat belonging to the sixteenth district (Shitangwan) of the county, while heading to the countryside to pump water for others yesterday afternoon, collided with the pier of the Huadu Bridge near Luoshe, causing half of the bridge to collapse. The falling bricks and stones crushed the boat, causing it to sink immediately due to the weight. Fortunately, no one was injured. Currently, both water and land transportation have been blocked, causing considerable inconvenience to pedestrians.

Opening of Coffin for Re-Examination in the Yangshuyuan Homicide Case: Li Gong, wife of villager Li Zhilin from the Yangshuyuan area, District Sixteen (Wan'an City), suddenly disappeared on the evening of May 30th. The next day, her body was found in the river. Prosecutor Zhu from the county court led officials to the village for an inspection, which determined that she had drowned and there were no visible injuries. However, Gong's father, Gong Gentang, insisted that his daughter was beaten to death by her husband, Li Zhilin, and petitioned the High Court for another investigation to redress the injustice. After reviewing the case files, the High Court ordered the local county court prosecutor's office to summon the victim's family and witnesses for questioning. Yesterday, Chief Judge Zhou summoned the plaintiff, defendant, and witnesses to court for questioning. He then ordered the victim's family to transport Li Gong's coffin to the city by boat for a re-examination to determine the truth.

Jingjiang

Resolution of Dispute Between Two Bus Companies: The Jingtai Public Bus Company and the Lijing Long-Distance Bus Company were engaged in a competitive dispute. On the 16th, Jingtai gathered a large group to petition the party and government agencies, demanding the detention of Lijing's military vehicles. To maintain amicable relations between the two companies, County Magistrate Chen Guiqing invited representatives from both companies, as well as the Construction Bureau, Public Security Bureau, and County Party Headquarters, to a meeting at the county government. After repeated mediation, it was decided that the companies would operate on alternate days. Jingtai would operate for seventeen days each month, and Lijing would operate for thirteen days, starting from the 18th and lasting until the end of August.

The Xingang Opium Bribery Case is Being Heard by the Zhenjiang Court: A large-scale opium case occurred in Xingang. The county government reported the case and brought Wei Sanguan, who was caught with the opium, in for questioning. However, the case was abruptly dismissed. Local residents, including Liu Zhenzhi, filed a complaint with the High Court, alleging that County Magistrate Wang Jiwu and Public Security Bureau Chief Jin Ming’an were suspected of accepting bribes and providing protection. After conducting an investigation, the High Court transferred the case to the Zhenjiang District Court for trial. The summonses have been sent to Jingjiang, and the summoned individuals include Wang Jiwu, Liang Wei, Liu Zhenzhi, Huang Weibang, Yao Zhusan, Xu Ming'en, Chen Chao, Lu Zhuoqun, Wang Jiadian, Lu Haoran, Liu Zancheng, Zhu Boyu, Du Zhihe, Zhu Zhongyi, and Ge Tianyi, a total of fifteen people. The court hearing is scheduled for 8:00 a.m. on the 24th.

Changzhou

Murder of Husband Case: Perpetrator Apprehended: Zhao Quangen, a farmer from Changxicun Village, about two li from Lihe Bridge in the second district of Wu County, was strangled to death last winter by his wife, Zhao Zhang, and Zhao Xiaolin. Zhao Guoming, a nephew of Quangen, filed a lawsuit with the court, accusing Zhao Zhang and Zhao Xiaolin of adultery and conspiring to murder Quangen. An autopsy confirmed that he had been strangled to death. However, the perpetrators were at large. Recently, the county court issued arrest warrants, and bailiff Ouyang Yunfa and others apprehended Zhao Xiaolin and Zhao Zhang on the 18th. After a preliminary hearing, they were ordered to be detained.

Continuation of the Mishandled Bone Setting Case: The case of negligence causing injury, in which the President of the Provincial Hospital, Wang Yuanchen, was sued by Yi Ruichang, the manager of a copper and tin shop, resumed hearing yesterday. The courtroom was crowded with onlookers. In addition to the plaintiff and defendant, the designated doctors from Hongren Hospital and the doctors who had treated the plaintiff were present. Judge Jin opened the court at 10:00 a.m. In addition to hiring lawyer Hu Zhen, the defendant also hired lawyer Peng Qi from Suzhou to defend him. First, the plaintiff, Yi Ruichang, stated that he had been admitted to the hospital last year to treat a leg fracture. The defendant had broken his leg bone while examining it, and the subsequent bone setting was unsuccessful, resulting in a disability. Wang Yuanchen argued that the breaking of the leg bone was due to Yi's syphilis, which made his bones fragile, and that imperfect bone setting was common in the medical field and he could not be held responsible. The plaintiff argued that since the defendant knew that the bone was fragile, he should have been careful and should not have broken it. Lawyer Peng argued that the time between the bone fracture and the filing of the lawsuit was more than six months, and that the initial complaint was not signed by the plaintiff himself, so the case was not valid. After the judge clarified the matter, it was determined that although the bone fracture occurred earlier, it took three months of bone setting before it was determined that it could not be healed. The plaintiff also admitted that the initial lawsuit was his intention. The assessor from Hongren Hospital stated that the set bone was indeed not aligned correctly. Due to bad weather, X-rays could not be taken, and only a rough diagram was drawn. As a result, the defendant requested another medical assessment with X-rays as evidence, and was willing to bear the costs to protect his reputation. The court agreed, and the court adjourned at 12:30 p.m.

Nantong

General Outline Salt Land Reclamation Company Holds Shareholders' Meeting: The General Outline Salt Land Reclamation Company of Shanggang held a shareholders' meeting on the 17th at the Youfei Hall in Nantong. Yu Qiren was elected chairman. It was resolved to reorganize the board of directors and supervisors. Yu Qiren, Liang Shoushan, Zhou Weibin, Mao Youren, Zhang Chubai, Lu Hanping, Zhuang Dezhi, Sun Weibin, and Zhang Mian were elected as directors. Zhu Jingci and Zhu Jiliu were elected as supervisors. It was also resolved that (1) the company's accumulated debt of over 130,000 yuan would be offset by dividing the company's Dayuan and Daheng district fields for compensation; (2) shareholders who had not paid the construction fees must pay them before October of this year; (3) former director Yao Zhongxun was urged to hand over all account books.

Collapse of Riverbank: Request for Relief from the Provincial Government: The Nantong riverbank has been collapsing more severely in recent days. On the 18th, the Riverbank Protection Association submitted a plan for surveying and constructing stone embankments, prepared by provincial and county committee members and representatives from all sectors, to the provincial government, requesting prompt relief. According to the provincial government's resolution, for necessary projects, the provincial treasury and local government would each raise half of the funds. In addition to the 25,000 yuan raised by the county, a request was made for the Finance Department to allocate 25,000 yuan to facilitate the project.

Provincial Government Prohibits Unauthorized Collection of Security Donations: Disputes have repeatedly arisen in various districts of Nantong due to the collection of security donations. The provincial government has ordered County Magistrate Zhang to ensure that security donations are not organized without the approval of the provincial government.

Rugao

Man Beaten to Death Due to Dam Issue: Conflicts arose between farmers from Haimen, employed by the Dayu Company in Jugang City, and the residents of Zhimawa over the issue of opening the dam. The tenants of the Dayu Company beat Cao Guifen, a resident of Zhimawa, to death and injured four or five others. The residents of the city were outraged and went on strike, refusing to resume business until the dam was opened to allow the accumulated water to flow into the sea. County Magistrate Qian Zuoyi, fearing the escalation of the situation, personally went to investigate on the 16th.

Yangzhou

Bandit Guo Shiying Arrested: Following the continuous robbery cases in Taifu Street and Xianliang Street in the city, the Jiangsu Pacification Superintendent's Office and the Department of Civil Affairs repeatedly ordered the Jiangdu County Government to strictly limit the time for solving the cases and recorded demerits against the responsible agencies. It has been learned that detectives Shao Shigui and others from the Police Brigade arrested a bandit named Guo Shiying (also known as Guo Xiaoerzi) in Xiaomaoshan, outside the North Gate of the city. After interrogation, Guo confessed that he and his accomplices Cao San, Wang Jinlong, and others (all residing in Zhenjiang) robbed Qiu Yongkang's home in Baocheng in March of the lunar calendar this year, and robbed the Qingsheng Rice Store and Qinghe Oil Shop in Xianliang Street in April. The detectives then went to Zhenjiang to arrest Cao and Wang, but both had already fled. Therefore, the brigade handed Guo over to the county for investigation today (the 18th).

Strict Order to Demolish Dikes and Embankments Illegally Occupying the Yue Lake: Farmers in the Tangjiapan and Laoguanzui areas of the tenth district of the county built dikes and embankments in the Yue Lake during the warlord era, reclaiming land from the water and eventually occupying it as their own property. The matter was reported to the Construction Committee, which repeatedly ordered the Jiangsu Provincial Construction Department to instruct the Jiangdu County Construction Bureau to jointly investigate and determine whether demolition was necessary. The owners who had illegally occupied the land were ordered to demolish the structures voluntarily, but they failed to comply. In April of this year, the county government ordered the 8th and 10th Public Security Sub-bureaus to enforce the demolition. However, Zhang Zhaozhi, Tan Dehong, and others came forward on behalf of the owners, requesting a temporary suspension due to the imminent wheat harvest and the high water level. The 10th District Office reported the situation to the county, which in turn reported it to the Construction Department for review, resulting in a delay in the demolition. The Jiangbei Canal Engineering Office's Jiangdu Section Works Office believes that the canal water level, which is still over one zhang and six chi despite the opening of the dams flowing into the Yangtze River, is affected by the illegal occupation of the Yue Lake through the construction of dikes and embankments in the Tangjiapan and Laoguanzui areas. It has submitted another request to the provincial government to order the demolition within a specified period. It has been learned that the county government received an order from the Construction Department yesterday, stating that the dikes and embankments were severely hindering water conservancy and had not been demolished to date, indicating negligence on the part of the county magistrate. The order instructs the 8th and 10th Public Security Sub-bureau chiefs to enforce the demolition and report the results for verification. Failure to comply will result in severe punishment for the sub-bureau chiefs.

Qingjiang

Rising River Water is Concerning: The amount of water flowing through the canals here has been increasing day by day. In addition to the salt canal being full after being diverted by the Shuangjin Sluice Gate, the Yangzhuang Small Dam was breached recently. The former course of the Yellow River, which had been silted up, is also full of water, overflowing onto the banks. The bridge boats at the North Gate and South Gate in Qingjiang are becoming insufficient. The Chamber of Commerce has purchased four bridge boats from the Huai'an Customs to add to the existing ones. The small steamship companies received a telegram from Zhenjiang yesterday, deciding to suspend the sale of long-distance downriver tickets tomorrow (the 16th). According to a telegram from Zhao Luqi, director of the Pizhou Dike Works Office, the water from Huai and Yi in the upper reaches is still rising, and the Qinfan Zhichun has reached two zhang and four chi. River affairs personnel who have witnessed the current situation cannot help but feel deeply concerned.

County Government Executes Four Bandits: The Huaiyin County Government, based on the report from the local Police Brigade, presented four bandits named Dong Degao, Su Guofu, Shao Weibang, and Shi Weixiang for adjudication. After interrogation, the bandits proved to be extremely cunning. However, after the victims Liu Bi and Chen Fu testified in court, the bandits Dong Degao, Su Guofu, and Shao Weibang confessed to the kidnapping and extortion of Liu Bi's family, and Shi Weixiang confessed to the kidnapping and extortion of Chen Fu's family. The county government telegraphed the provincial government for approval and was granted permission to execute the four bandits. Yesterday evening, the county government received the reply telegram. This morning (the 15th) at 10:00 a.m., County Magistrate He extracted the four men, verified their identities, bound them, and sent them to the execution ground outside the West Gate for execution by firing squad.

Jiashan

Silkworm Seed Farm Promotes Autumn Silkworms: The Jiashan Silkworm Seed Manufacturing Farm, located in Si Lane in the county seat, has been issuing Liqiu brand spring silkworm seeds since last year. The general rearing households have reported good harvests and have all welcomed the seeds. As a result, this year's spring silkworm seeds have already been set, and there are few remaining. The farm has recently seen the government's repeated promotion of autumn silkworms and intends to increase farmers' income by using discarded mulberry leaves and surplus labor. It has specially produced autumn silkworm seeds for sale. Each sheet of silkworm eggs can yield about thirty catties of cocoons, and the selling price is similar to that of spring silkworm cocoons. It is reported that the farm, fearing that there are not many autumn silkworm rearing households and no dedicated cocoon shops, has established its own cocoon shop to benefit silkworm farmers and promote the rearing of autumn silkworm cocoons produced by the farm.

Hangzhou

Eating Poisonous Mushrooms Leads to Two Deaths: In the Caojia Lane area of Yangfen, near Shangqianbu in Hang County, the wife of Li Jinsheng picked many fragrant mushrooms on the mountain yesterday. She brought them back to cook with mustard greens. Her mother came to visit and was invited to eat with them, using the mushrooms as a side dish. After eating, they suddenly complained of abdominal pain. Jinsheng returned home and, seeing the situation, realized they had been poisoned. He hired people to carry his mother-in-law back to Fengjiaqiao in Dongtang. Before they reached home, she died from the poison. His wife also died after medical treatment failed. Several other farmers in the area had also eaten the mushrooms, but fortunately they vomited them out and were unharmed. Chickens and ducks that ate the vomit also died. The police station has been notified to ban the picking of the mushrooms.

Zhejiang Foil Tax Bureau to be Abolished: The revenue of Zhejiang Province in the 20th year of the Republic is severely insufficient. The Finance Department has decided that the annual expenditure of the Foil Tax Bureau is about 30,000 yuan. This special tax has always been handled by the foil shop operators in Shaoxing, and the bureau is only responsible for supervision. The duties are extremely simple. With the current financial difficulties in the province and the implementation of austerity measures, the bureau is deemed unnecessary. An order has been issued to wind up the affairs of the bureau, and it will be abolished from next month.

Ningbo

Robbery and Assault Case Occurs in Huang Guolin: Zhao Feng's small money shop in Shenjiao Village, near Huang Guolin in Yin County, was doing reasonably well. Around 8:00 p.m. last night, five or six bandits speaking in mixed dialects and wearing short, solid-color clothes suddenly broke in. One bandit pulled out a pistol and demanded silence, while the others held wooden sticks and cut all the telephone lines. Fortunately, it was still early, and a neighbor alerted the police by ringing a gong. The bandits panicked and fled southeast. It is reported that the loss was not significant, about thirty yuan. However, a neighbor named Zhou was shot in the foot, and two shop assistants were also injured by the wooden sticks. After hearing the news, the Huang Guolin Public Security Bureau dispatched police to pursue the bandits.

Xiaoshan

Forty-One Villages in Tianle Vie for the Linpu Police District: A dispute has arisen between Xiaoshan and Shaoxing counties over the issue of the Linpu Town police district. Xiaoshan County Magistrate Du submitted a request to the Department of Civil Affairs for approval to include the entire town of the police district in Xiaoshan County in order to unify administration. However, Shao County Public Security Bureau Chief Mo Rundong initially disagreed, arguing that the old boundaries should be maintained and there was no need to separate them. Now, forty-one villages in Tianle Township have issued a declaration and telegraphed the provincial government, stating their reasons and requesting the Shaoxing Association in Hangzhou to forward their concerns. They are protesting County Magistrate Du of Xiaoshan's encroachment on Shaoxing County's police governance rights. As a result, the opinions have deepened, and the case is becoming more difficult to resolve.

Husband and Wife Electrocuted Simultaneously: On the evening of the 18th, two farmers, Mo Zhaoyou and others, from the Caiyu Bridge area outside the South Gate of Xiaoshan, were returning home from working in the fields when they encountered heavy rain and lightning. The farmers were electrocuted to death. Unexpectedly, his wife, who was visiting relatives, was returning home at the same time and was also electrocuted to death by the field. The two were about one li apart and were both struck by lightning. This is truly a strange occurrence.

Clothes Transport Boat Robbed: At midnight on the 18th, a night boat traveling from Shaoxing to Xiaoshan near Qianqing and Xiaoyangzhou on the West Xiaojiang was forced ashore and robbed by five bandits disguised as passengers. The bandits looted the passengers' luggage and money, totaling over one hundred yuan. They also stole over twenty catties of white silk and several bolts of satin. They fired shots in the air as a warning and fled towards Guantang Road.

Qu County

New and Old County Magistrates Hand Over: Xu Zhigui, the county magistrate of Qu County, has been transferred by the Zhejiang Provincial Government, and the vacancy will be filled by Wu Bokuan. It has been learned that County Magistrate Wu arrived in Qu County on the 14th and is scheduled to take over on the 17th. Local people and agencies in the county who know County Magistrate Wu's past history are very welcome. They have been visiting him and providing detailed accounts of the local matters that need to be promoted and reformed.

Letter

Letter from Pei Xiyu of the Wuhu District Court Procuratorate

To the esteemed Editor,

I have recently read a news item in your newspaper's foreign news section (July 4th) titled "Major Upheaval in Wuhu's Legal Circles." I would like to point out the following inaccuracies regarding my reputation: (1) Our court issues arrest warrants with limited validity periods. Arrest warrants are different from wanted notices. If an arrest cannot be made, the bailiff should return the arrest warrant for cancellation. Wanted notices, on the other hand, have no expiration date. This is clear to anyone with basic legal knowledge and is a common practice in all courts. The arrest warrants issued in the Mingxing case, which I handled, were all returned for cancellation because the individuals could not be found. The case files are all available for verification. This is one inaccuracy in your newspaper's report. (2) Prosecutors can only exercise prosecutorial powers. Fines and detention are judicial powers and are the responsibility of the judges. I would never dare to overstep my authority. Your newspaper's report that Peng Songqing's assault case was only fined and not detained is something that someone familiar with the law would not say. In conclusion, the higher authorities have sent personnel to thoroughly investigate this case, and the truth will be determined. It is inappropriate to damage my reputation based on one-sided accounts. I fear that the rumors are inaccurate and have written to request a correction. I hope this is granted.

Sincerely,

Pei Xiyu, Prosecutor of the Wuhu District Court

July 16th

Local News

Anti-Japanese Aid to Overseas Chinese Association Prepares to Mourn Dead Overseas Chinese Compatriots

▲ Scheduled to be held at the Municipal Chamber of Commerce on the 23rd

▲ The entire city will fly flags at half-mast and close for half a day

▲ Eleven committee members are designated to form a preparatory committee

The Shanghai Anti-Japanese Aid to Overseas Chinese Committee, after its first committee meeting, decided to hold a memorial service for the dead overseas Chinese compatriots on the 23rd of this month. The committee members will also take their oaths of office on that day to show their anti-Japanese resolve. The preparations are currently underway. The following are the latest news reports:

▲ Formation of the Preparatory Committee: The committee, after its first executive meeting, decided to organize a preparatory committee to actively prepare for the event. Yesterday, letters were sent to all the preparatory committee members, scheduling a meeting for today (the 20th) at 4:00 p.m. The letter reads as follows: "To the esteemed, as per the resolution of the first committee meeting of this association, the memorial service for the dead overseas Chinese compatriots is scheduled for the 23rd of this month (Thursday) morning. Flags will be flown at half-mast throughout the city, and businesses will be closed for half a day. The committee members will also take their oaths of office at 9:00 a.m. on that day. However, the matter is important and time is short, so preparations must be made in advance. The first executive meeting of this association has decided to organize a preparatory committee, and Zhu Xuefan, Wang Wenhua, Zheng Mingfa, Yu Hualong, Zhang Yichen, Hu Fengxiang, Lin Kecong, Cheng Zhusun, Lu Xingzhuang, Feng Yixian, and Tang Junsheng have been designated as the eleven preparatory committee members, with Zheng Mingfa designated as the convener of the committee. The first preparatory meeting will be held at the Municipal Chamber of Commerce's regular meeting room at 4:00 p.m. on the 20th of this month to discuss the way forward. We hope that you will attend and participate in the discussions."

▲ Filing for Record: The committee submitted a report to the Municipal Party Headquarters, the Municipal Government, and the Social Affairs Bureau yesterday, stating: "Report for filing. At the first committee meeting of this association on the 17th of this month, the holding of a memorial service for the dead overseas Chinese compatriots and the taking of oaths of office by the committee members were discussed. It was decided to hold the event at the Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce at 9:00 a.m. on July 23rd. Businesses will be closed throughout the city for half a day on the morning of the event, and flags will be flown at half-mast to express mourning. The matter is hereby recorded and reported for your review and filing. Please notify all industrial and commercial organizations in the city to comply (for the Party Headquarters), and please send representatives to supervise the oath-taking ceremony on that day to show solemnity."

▲ Letters to Various Organizations: Letters were also sent to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, the Federation of Exchanges, the Banking Association, the Money Industry Association, the Citizens' Federation, and the Ratepayers' Association of the Two Concessions, stating: (1) "To the esteemed, at the first committee meeting of this association on the 17th of this month, the holding of a memorial service for the dead overseas Chinese compatriots and the taking of oaths of office by the committee members were discussed. It was decided to hold the event at the Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce at 9:00 a.m. on July 23rd (Thursday). Businesses will be closed throughout the city for half a day on the morning of the event, and flags will be flown at half-mast to express mourning. In addition to reporting the matter to the Municipal Party Headquarters and the Municipal Government for review and filing, we are sending this letter to the Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce to notify all industries to comply. We request that your association notify all members to fly flags at half-mast throughout the day and close for half a day in the morning to show unity and express mourning. As this matter concerns external representation, we request that you take note and act accordingly." (2) "To the esteemed, as per the resolution of the first committee meeting of this association on the 17th of this month, the holding of a memorial service for the dead overseas Chinese compatriots and the taking of oaths of office by the committee members were discussed. It was decided to hold the event in your association's conference hall at 9:00 a.m. on July 23rd (Thursday). Businesses will be closed throughout the city for half a day on the morning of the event, and flags will be flown at half-mast to express mourning. We are sending this letter to request the use of your association's conference hall and to request that you notify all members and businesses in the city to close for half a day in the morning and fly the national flag throughout the day to show unity and express mourning. We address this to the Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce."

▲ Fundraising Telegram: The committee continued to send a telegram yesterday regarding fundraising for relief efforts, stating: "To fellow compatriots at home and abroad, during this incident, overseas Chinese in Korea were persecuted by the Japanese-instigated Koreans, resulting in thousands of deaths and injuries and tens of thousands of unemployed. The cruelty and suffering cannot be described. Relief and comfort require substantial funds. We believe that overseas Chinese have contributed greatly to the revolution and nation-building. Whenever there are tragedies and disasters in the country, they contribute generously and take the lead. Now that the overseas Chinese in Korea have suffered the tragedy of being massacred and destroyed, we, the compatriots of the whole country, should rush to their aid. The first committee meeting of this association has decided to send a telegram to home and abroad to raise relief funds and to establish an economic committee to be responsible for safekeeping. Qin Runqing, Chen Guangfu, Zhang Zhiqian, Xu Jilun, Qian Xinzhi, Xi Yushu, Wang Yansong, and others have been designated as committee members, and the Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce, the Central Bank, the Bank of China, the Bank of Communications, the Zhejiang Industrial Bank, the Shanghai Commercial & Savings Bank, the Savings Association of the Four Banks, and the Fuyuan Money Exchange have been designated as collection agencies. We urge fellow compatriots at home and abroad to respond with a sense of urgency and a spirit of generosity and contribute generously. As soon as the funds are collected, they will be remitted immediately. We respectfully telegraph this request, hoping that you will take note.

Yu Qiaqing, Chairman of the Shanghai Anti-Japanese Aid to Overseas Chinese Committee, and Standing Committee Members Wang Xiaolai, Wang Yansong, Tao Baichuan, Hou Dachun, Chen Tingrui, and Lu Jingshi jointly announce."

Active Promotion of Boycotting Japanese Goods Amidst Anti-Japanese Sentiments

▲ Strict Measures to be Taken Against New Orders

▲ Design Committee to Convene Tomorrow

Following resolutions passed by the Anti-Japanese Aid China Association and the Municipal Chamber of Commerce to sever economic ties with Japan, active measures are underway. All plans are being implemented based on effective and sustainable principles. Furthermore, the Association has found instances of backdating order forms for recent goods ordered, which is considered a betrayal of the nation. The Association will take the strictest measures against these goods. The following is a summary of news gathered yesterday:

▲ Design Meeting: The first executive meeting of the Anti-Japanese Aid China Association resolved to establish a Design Committee, including economic experts, business leaders, and key figures from customs brokerage and transportation industries. The committee will consist of nine to twenty-seven members. Eleven members have already been nominated, including Li Quanshi, Zhu Yinong, and Chen Songyuan. It is reported that Chen Songyuan, the convener of the committee, recognizing the urgency of the design process, has scheduled the first Design Meeting for 4:00 PM on the 21st to formulate concrete plans for boycotting Japanese goods. These plans will be submitted to the full committee for deliberation and implementation.

▲ Letter to the Chamber of Commerce: The Anti-Japanese Aid China Association sent a letter to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce yesterday, stating: "Regarding the guiding principles for dealing with Japanese goods, as resolved in the first meeting of our committee, (A) goods already ordered should be returned promptly; (B) goods ordered but not yet arrived at the port should have shipments halted; (C) goods already in warehouses but not yet paid for should not be claimed; (D) goods already purchased should be registered with the Association first and temporarily suspended from distribution. Those who violate the above four measures will be severely punished according to the stipulated disciplinary regulations." Aside from the registration rules and disciplinary regulations which are being drafted and will be announced later, we are first sending the handling measures for your records, urging your esteemed Chamber to promptly inform all businesses in the city to comply in unison to avoid any delays. Addressed to the Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce.

▲ Strict Investigation of Japanese Goods: The Anti-Japanese Aid China Association sent letters to customs brokers, dockworkers, and industrial and commercial groups yesterday, stating: "The recent massacre of overseas Chinese compatriots by Koreans instigated by the Japanese has aroused righteous indignation among all Chinese people. Therefore, all sectors of this city have unanimously resolved to permanently sever economic ties with Japan to demonstrate our ultimate determination. If any Chinese person possesses even a shred of conscience, they should be inspired to act in unison. However, news reports indicate that some opportunistic and treacherous merchants are taking advantage of the situation to purchase Japanese goods, sacrificing the blood of our overseas Chinese compatriots to enrich themselves. If this is permissible, what is not? Your associations are undoubtedly familiar with the movement of goods through customs declarations and loading/unloading. In addition to assigning personnel to secretly investigate, we hereby inform you that any purchases of Japanese goods should be reported to this Association at any time for investigation and handling. The success of the Anti-Japanese Movement relies on this." Addressed to the Customs Brokers Association, Customs Brokerage Industry Association, Dockworkers Union, and Transportation Industry Association.

▲ Party Headquarters' Recommendations: In light of the failures of past anti-Japanese efforts, the Third District Party Headquarters, after its twelfth meeting, resolved on seven measures to recommend to the Municipal Executive Committee, instructing the Anti-Japanese Aid China Association to comply. The following are excerpts of the measures: (1) All Japanese goods seized should be burned and no funds should be collected; (2) The handling of seized goods should not exceed three days; responsible individuals will be subject to sanctions by the Supervisory Committee if the deadline is missed; (3) Those who offer bribes and confess will have the bribe money returned by the Association; if they do not confess and are reported, the bribe money will be used as a reward for the informant, and the briber will be punished equally with the recipient of the bribe; (4) Regardless of the amount of the bribe, if there is solid evidence or witnesses, the recipient should be immediately executed; (5) Disciplinary regulations, handling measures, and organizational outlines should be approved and implemented by the All-Circles Representatives Assembly; (6) All Japanese goods seized daily must be published in newspapers; (7) The All-Circles Representatives Assembly must be convened once a month. It is reported that a statement of reasons has been prepared and submitted to the Municipal Executive Committee.

▲ Discussions in Various Sectors: (1) The Customs Brokers Association has scheduled a meeting to discuss measures to refuse to declare Japanese goods; (2) The Cotton Cloth Trade Association has scheduled a meeting for 2:00 PM on July 22nd to discuss voluntary boycott measures during the second session of its general assembly; (3) Announcement (No. 4) from the Silk Thread Industry Association to its members: Regarding an urgent announcement, according to reports on the 16th of this month, "The Shanghai All-Circles Anti-Japanese Aid China Assembly declared that, based on the resolutions of the All-Circles Assembly on the 13th of this month, an economic severance with Japan will be strictly enforced from today onwards. If anyone privately imports Japanese goods after the 14th, they will be subject to the strictest sanctions according to the measures to be decided in the future. Please pay close attention." The Wanbaoshan Massacre of overseas Chinese compatriots is entirely the beginning of the Japanese imperialist plan to invade our country, which is still progressing. The conspiracy is being widely reported, and the whole country is indignant. The business community of this city has voluntarily initiated a joint organization of industrial, commercial, and academic circles to form the Anti-Japanese Aid China Assembly to unanimously carry out the economic severance with Japan, as a backing for government negotiations. This association deeply sympathizes with this patriotic action. The third executive committee meeting on the 16th of this month resolved to notify all members that all Japanese goods ordered and currently in stock as of the 16th of this month must be reported to this association with detailed information on the name and quantity of the goods within one week (by the 24th of this month) for verification during inspections. From the 17th of this month onwards, no further orders or purchases of Japanese goods are allowed, except for previously ordered goods. Otherwise, this association will not be responsible. In addition to separate notifications, members are urged to fill out the registration form and submit it, and avoid making mistakes that may lead to severe penalties. This is extremely important. This announcement is hereby made. (Attached registration form). July 16th, 20th year of the Republic of China, Chairman Zhang Yuanxiong.

Conclusion of the Social Affairs Bureau Factory Inspection

▲ Currently Sorting and Categorizing and Creating Tables

▲ To Prepare for the Implementation of the Factory Law

The National Government has decided that the Factory Law and the Regulations for the Implementation of the Factory Law will be implemented on August 1st. In order to prepare for the implementation of the Factory Law, the Social Affairs Bureau of this city established a factory inspection in January of this year. More than ten industries, including papermaking, matches, enamel, cotton spinning, machinery, silk reeling, and oil pressing, have been inspected. Now that the implementation date of the Factory Law is approaching, the inspection was stopped from the previous day and is being concluded. In recent days, the bureau has been sorting and categorizing to create tables to serve as a reference for the implementation of the Factory Law and factory inspections. The table of contents is as follows: (1) Factories in each industry; (2) Age of workers; (3) Illegal work in each industry; (4) Working hours, breaks, and holidays; (5) Wage matters in each industry; (6) Worker welfare undertakings; (7) Subsidies and compensation; (8) Work contracts, factory rules, leave procedures, and work rewards and punishments.

Resolution of the Dock Dues Dispute Between the Cotton Cloth, Customs Declaration, and Dock Industries

▲ Entrusted to the Cotton Cloth Industry by the Hakka

▲ Cotton Cloth Association Notifies Members to Comply

The dispute between the cotton cloth and customs declaration industries over the collection of dock dues was mediated by the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau without success, and the Municipal Chamber of Commerce was instructed to handle it properly. The Chamber repeatedly convened all parties for mediation. The cotton cloth industry refused to collect the dues because the dock dues had to be borne by the Hakka merchants. The customs declaration industry also refused to collect the dues because dock dues were traditionally included in the price of goods. The Hakka merchants, due to the lack of manpower to handle business matters, proposed entrusting the cotton cloth industry to handle the procedures for paying the dues. All parties insisted, and the dispute could not be resolved. The Chamber had no choice but to formulate a plan and report it to the Social Affairs Bureau for review. The Bureau, based on the handling of the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, instructed the Hakka and Cotton Cloth Industry Association to comply. Now the Cotton Cloth Association has resolved to comply with the order, and the dispute can finally be resolved. The details of each situation are recorded below:

▲ Order from the Social Affairs Bureau: The Municipal Social Affairs Bureau instructed the Cotton Cloth Industry Association to comply, stating: "Regarding the issue of dock dues payment, the customs declaration and cotton cloth industries have been shirking responsibility. The Bureau previously ordered the Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce to investigate the responsibility of the business and mediate properly. According to the Chamber's report, the mediation has not been successful, and two measures are proposed: (1) The Hakka can entrust the cotton cloth industry to handle the procedures for paying dock dues; (2) The Hakka must be responsible for paying the full amount of the dues paid by the cotton cloth industry on their behalf and must not be short. Based on the review, the proposed measures are appropriate and should be approved. In addition to ordering the Hakka cotton cloth merchants to add one mace and three candareens of silver dock dues per single package and two mace and six candareens of silver per double package when paying the unified tax and additional fees, and to hand them over to the industry's firms for payment, the Association is ordered to inform the firms to comply and collect and pay the dues on their behalf. This is important." At the same time, the Sichuan, Shandong, Yantai, and Harbin merchants are ordered to comply.

▲ Letter from the Cotton Cloth Industry: The Cotton Cloth Industry Association convened the Executive Committee on the 18th to discuss dock dues. All committee members, including Chen Songyuan, attended and resolved to comply with the order from the Social Affairs Bureau. Yesterday, the Association notified its members, stating: "This Association was previously instructed by the Social Affairs Bureau on the 4th and 17th to inform its members that, from today onwards, an additional transportation fee (i.e., cartage) of three mace and four candareens of silver must be collected from the Hakka merchants for each piece of cotton cloth, and transferred to the customs declaration workers to alleviate their hardships, in accordance with past practice. On the 17th of this month, we continued to receive the order, stating: (Omitted) Since the outbreak of this case, responsible personnel within the Association have been running around and appealing, and sending letters and telegrams. It has taken months and accumulated volumes of documents to finally come to an end. If any of our members sell cotton cloth to the Hakka merchants in the future, they must comply with the Bureau's order and collect an additional six mace of silver for cartage dock dues for each double package and three mace of silver for each single package, in addition to the price of goods and unified tax, in order to comply with the official order and facilitate payment on their behalf. Please do not deviate or make mistakes. This is extremely important. This announcement is hereby made."

Pilot Strike Awaits Resolution at Today's Meeting

▲ Members Insist on Not Resuming Work Unconditionally

Regarding the pilot strike involving foreign ships in Shanghai, after the Consular Body of the Jianghai Customs and the joint associations of British and American chambers of commerce held a joint meeting, they decided to order all members of the Pilot Association to resume work unconditionally starting today. When the Association received the notification from the Jianghai Customs, it had a meeting, but because of the short time and the different opinions of the members on the letter from the Jianghai Customs, the meeting on the afternoon before yesterday only reported the contents of the letter from the Jianghai Customs and did not vote. Yesterday was a Sunday and no formal meeting was convened. Only informal contacts were made between members. Whether to accept the letter from the Jianghai Customs and resume work will be discussed and resolved at a meeting at 9:30 AM today at the Association's office at No. 26, The Bund. The situation yesterday is recorded below:

▲ Contact Between Members: Yesterday was a Sunday, and no members attended the meeting, nor was there a formal meeting. However, there were some contacts between members. It was vaguely heard that they mostly suggested that if the three groups of the Jianghai Customs, etc., could agree to consider the one shilling and eight pence as the minimum pilotage fee after they resumed work, and then give a reasonable reply, the members would be willing to resume work first. Otherwise, the members all expressed dissatisfaction with the unconditional resumption of work as stated by Mr. Green, the port director of the Jianghai Customs.

▲ Pilot License: Regarding the re-issuance of pilot licenses that have been cancelled by the Jianghai Customs, a key official of the Customs said that it would probably be issued after receiving the reply from the Pilot Association today.

▲ American Consulate's Statement: A reporter from Xinsheng News interviewed the American Consul General who attended the joint meeting of the three groups yesterday and asked about the document received by the American Consulate from Mr. Green, the port director of the Jianghai Customs, regarding the pilot strike, and the three groups' handling of the Pilot Association if it does not accept the resumption of work. He replied that he had not yet received Mr. Green's document, so he could not comment. The unconditional order for the pilots to resume work was indeed decided by the meeting, but he could not be sure what would happen if the Pilot Association did not accept it.

Municipal Social Affairs Bureau Prevents Foreign Fishing Vessels from Registering Under False Names

▲ Drafted Measures to Submit to the Municipal Government for Approval

After the Japanese fishing vessels that encroached on fishing in Shanghai were investigated by the Customs Anti-Smuggling Department and the Naval Department's Coast Defense Patrol Office, and the vessels were dispatched to strictly inspect the waters outside the Wusongkou for Japanese fishing vessels privately smuggling, they have now disappeared. In order to prevent foreign fishing vessels from colluding with unscrupulous merchants to register under false names, the Shanghai Municipal Fisheries Guidance Center has drafted a total of ten measures to prevent and punish, detailing the reasons, and submitted them to the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau for review. After review, the Bureau has now submitted the report to the Municipal Government for approval. Once approved by the Municipal Government, the measures will be implemented.

Chen Fugen Found Not Guilty in Extortion Case

▲ Still Sent to Public Security Bureau for Further Verification

Chen Bingxiang, a Guangdong resident residing at 212 Miller Road, was kidnapped by bandits around 9 PM on June 17th on Morrison Road. Chen was quick-witted and escaped on the spot. However, from the 21st to the 27th of the same month, he successively received threatening letters from the bandit gang, demanding 18,000 yuan. They arranged a meeting inside the Shenchun Auto Shop lane on Connaught Road, requiring the money, wrapped in paper, to be thrown into a trash can in the lane, from where someone would retrieve it. Chen immediately reported this to the Hongkou Police Station, which dispatched detectives and arrested a suspect, Chen Fugen, a local. When questioned by the Special District Court, he denied the charges and retained Lawyer Da Yaoxian for his defense. The court ordered a date for the verdict. Yesterday, Judge Xiao presided over the Third Court and ruled Chen Fugen not guilty. Lawyer Li, representing the police station, stated that Chen Fugen was initially handed over to the police station by the Shanghai Six-Counties Public Security Bureau. Chen is now to be sent back to the Bureau, which the court approved.

Street Construction in Sanlin Town

The streets of Sanlin Town, Shanghai County's Fourth District, have been in disrepair for years. Bricks and stones are loose and the surface is uneven, causing extreme inconvenience for travelers. Last year, the town's district office sent a detailed survey request to the County Construction Bureau and drafted a widening plan. The Municipal Construction Committee also resolved on construction methods. Now, gentlemen from both inside and outside the district, including Tang Zichun, Zhang Shangyi, Zhou Tingxiu, Kang Xitao, Jin Liren, and Huo Guozhen, have initiated a fundraising campaign to carry out the construction. Yesterday, the first design committee meeting was held to discuss the implementation plan. Those present included the initiators Zhang Shangyi (represented by Cai Jun), Tang Zichun, Huo Guozhen, Kang Xitao (represented by Huo Wenxiang), as well as the Public Security Bureau Chief Zhang Zhenyuan, District Chief Bi Xinzhai, County Party Department member Ding Renke, Town Chief Huo Guiliang, Yang Zhiqiang, Zhu Ruoquan, and more than ten others. District Chief Bi was elected as chairman. The following resolutions were passed: (1) Tang Zichun was elected as the road construction director; (2) Road construction materials will be the responsibility of Mr. Tang to negotiate, with assistance from the County Construction Bureau; (3) Funding will be divided into special donations (initiated by the responsible fundraisers), frontage donations (from property owners), and shop donations (from the Chamber of Commerce). These will be initiated today.

Paint Apprentice Dies from Fall

Yesterday afternoon at around 4:20 PM, painting work was in progress inside the Bund's Bank of China. A paint apprentice, Chen Yunchang, 17 years old, accidentally lost his footing and fell from a ladder, injuring his head. He was barely breathing. Someone called the police from 3243 Street, who transported him to Renji Hospital. He died despite emergency treatment. The hospital transferred the body to the coroner's office to await examination by the court.

Pedestrian Struck by Tram in French Concession

At 8 PM last night, Car No. 14, a Route 5 tram traveling from Ximen to the Shanghai-Nanjing Railway Station, was proceeding from Ximen towards the Siming Guild Hall behind the Xinxin Bridge Street in the French Concession. A man, approximately 40 years old, wearing a silk short jacket and trousers, was walking from south to north. As the tram approached, he was unable to avoid it and was struck. He suffered injuries to his left arm, head, and face, bleeding profusely. Fortunately, the Taiping Board pried him free, preventing amputation, but he was already unconscious. French-Vietnamese police arrived and transported the injured man and the tram to Renji Hospital for treatment. Reports suggest his injuries are severe and he may not survive.

Promotion of New Weights and Measures Cannot Be Delayed

The Municipal Chamber of Commerce, regarding the implementation date of the new weights and measures system, deemed it inappropriate to request a postponement and sent a letter to the Oil Pressing Industry Association, stating: "Regarding your letter of the 16th requesting a transfer to the Social Affairs Bureau to postpone the implementation of the new weights and measures system for your industry until February 1st of the following year: This matter was discussed and resolved at the members' meeting on June 27th to request the Social Affairs Bureau to determine the implementation period of the new weights and measures system, and to temporarily exempt from inspection during the implementation period. Considering the situation, the implementation of the new system in our city is included in the first phase and has already been approved by the former Ministry of Industry and Commerce. The unified weights and measures procedures set by our city were jointly determined by the Municipal Government and the former Ministry of Industry and Commerce as early as May of the 19th year. It is extremely difficult to overturn the decision made more than a year ago and request a postponement again. Therefore, after careful consideration, we had no choice but to make a temporary request for an implementation period, hoping for a transitional and gradual approach to avoid excessive conflicts. We subsequently received a reply from the Social Affairs Bureau stating that the inspection period set by our city was originally divided into three phases, with the first phase running from July 11th to September 26th, providing ample time for preparation. Zhabei is included in the second phase, and the Special District (i.e., the Concession) is included in the third phase, allowing even more time for preparation. Therefore, the inspection period is the implementation period and does not need to be determined separately. Furthermore, the punishment measures during inspection will not be strictly enforced. We have already copied the entire text of this order and issued a separate notice. As for industries such as salted meat, where foreign weights and measures are still using the old system, making transactions difficult, this association has also reported to the Social Affairs Bureau to be forwarded to the Ministry of Industry for verification. The situation described by your association is largely the same. We should wait for the Social Affairs Bureau to receive the Ministry's approval and forward it to the association before issuing a further notice. The request for a postponement is based on the above-mentioned circumstances and is indeed inconvenient to forward."

Page 12

Municipal Chamber of Commerce Requests Promotion of Chinese Merchant Notary Services

The Municipal Chamber of Commerce submitted a request to the Ministry of Industry yesterday, stating that the notary public business should be staffed by Chinese merchants: "Regarding the request: At the members' meeting held by this association on June 27th, member representatives of the Huashang Yizhong Auction House, Luo Qinghua, Zhu Wenqi, Jiang Zigang, Shao Baoxing, Fang Jiaobo, Ge Jechen, and Zheng Chengqing, proposed the following: The fire insurance industry originated in European countries as a means of ensuring safety, which is an excellent practice. It has been promoted in our country for decades, but all methods are based on foreign merchants, and the insurance policies and articles of association used are all in foreign languages. The wording often favors one side over the other, so when an accident occurs and compensation is due, disputes often arise between the insured and the insurer. To impartially arbitrate these disputes, a third party must step in, the so-called notary public. Therefore, the notary public is extremely important to the interests and legal status of both parties. In European and American countries, those who engage in notary public duties must first be specially licensed by the government, given a business license, and registered with the government office before they can perform their duties. Foreign merchant notary firms, in their capacity as foreign notaries public, perform notary public services within our country without the permission of our government or any government office, regardless of whether they have a notary public license. Although they are called notaries public, they are in reality representatives of foreign merchant insurance companies. Their judgments and estimations invariably favor the insurer, imposing compulsory measures and not allowing our Chinese people to intervene. Countless Chinese merchants have suffered as a result. There are even cases where accidents occurred several years ago, but foreign merchant notaries public have refused to pay compensation, citing non-compliance with the articles of association. A notary public has the nature of arbitration and exercises the power of appraisal, and must have the special permission of the state or government office. There is no reason why foreign merchants can arbitrarily exercise this authority within our country. Unfortunately, our country's previous administrative authorities did not examine this carefully and allowed foreign merchants to hold this position for decades. On the one hand, this was due to the lack of a Chinese organization for this business. Now that the period of political tutelage has begun and legal rights are being actively recovered, lawyers, accountants, and other professionals from foreign countries have been gradually restricted, but no measures have yet been taken to rectify this notary public function. Previously, this association, due to the fact that foreign merchant insurance companies often used biased notaries public to avoid paying insurance claims, notified all industries to no longer take out insurance with foreign merchant companies. This shows that the notary public function is closely related to the interests of all industries. Therefore, it is formally proposed at this congress that, in the future, when Chinese policyholders encounter accidents, regardless of whether the insurance company is Chinese or foreign, if a notary public is required for arbitration, it should be handled by a Chinese merchant notary public who has registered with the government. If the insurance company hires a foreign merchant notary public, the Chinese policyholder should refuse. This method can be requested to be stated on the insurance policy when it is issued. It is also requested that the Ministry of Industry issue a general order to all relevant government offices and commercial organizations to comply with this, and issue an order to the governments of all provinces and cities to order foreign merchant notaries public to cease their duties when they are exercising their functions within our country. Furthermore, our company organized the Yizhong Auction House in the 16th year of the Republic of China, concurrently operating a notary public business, being the sole pioneer of Chinese notaries public. We have already presented this to the former Shanghai Political Sub-Council, the National Registration Bureau, and the Shanghai Municipal Social Affairs Bureau for registration and filing, to protect and promote it. We have also been appointed as appraisers by the Shanghai Local Court and the Shanghai Special District Court in various cases. All Chinese merchant insurance companies have our company handle their notary public affairs. Therefore, we request that the Ministry of Industry separately circulate for verification the information regarding our company's existing notary public status and history, so as to promote it, which would be extremely fortunate. According to current international practice, there are restrictions on foreigners holding public office in other countries, and Japan's prohibitions are even stricter, absolutely not allowing foreigners to hold such positions. Our country has treated this as an ordinary occupation in the commercial arena and has not paid attention, and without careful examination, the commercial losses have been enormous. In recent years, Chinese merchants have gradually learned to imitate this practice, but because foreign merchant insurance companies have a strong foundation and foreign merchant notaries public work in unison, they are still in their grasp. Unless the government clearly stipulates laws and regulations, implements registration methods, and establishes the principle that Chinese merchants should fill the position of notary public, it will be difficult to reverse the accumulated momentum. Based on the above reasons, it was resolved at the members' meeting of this association on June 27th to submit this request for review. We have prepared the documents and respectfully request that your Ministry examine and approve this, clearly stipulate the methods, and issue a general order to all provinces and cities to follow suit, which would be for the public good."

Domestic Import and Export of Native Goods Exempt from Dredging Tax

Loford, the Jianghai Customs Tax Officer, issued proclamation No. 1220 yesterday: "Regarding the proclamation: We have received an order from the Inspector General of Customs stating that all native goods imported from domestic ports and exported from this port to domestic ports will be exempt from the dredging tax from July 20th of this year. We must comply with this order. We hereby notify all merchants and people to be aware of this. This is hereby proclaimed."

Liquor and Tobacco Industries Oppose Tax-Farming Conference

▲ Two Resolutions Passed

The local public associations of Shanghai, including the distilleries, Shaoxing wine industry, local yellow wine industry, silk floss tobacco industry, Fenjiu wine industry, sauce garden industry, western tobacco industry, tobacco leaf industry, and dry tobacco industry, held an emergency meeting yesterday (the 19th) at the Fenjiu Wine Industry Association on Fangxie Road, Ximen, in Jiping Lane, regarding the practice of tax farming for liquor and tobacco licenses, private tax increases, violations of superior orders, and harassment of merchants and people. They resolved: (1) That each public association jointly request the Municipal Chamber of Commerce to forward a request to the provincial bureau to abolish the tax farming system and private increases; (2) That each public association notify its members to submit their licenses to the association for consolidated payment, and designate the Fenjiu Wine Industry Association to draft and lead the effort, with each public association mutually electing one official to jointly take responsibility for the process, with the intention of continuing the action until the abolition is achieved.

Ministry of Industry Focuses on Industrial Standards

▲ Letter from the Bureau of Industry and Commerce to Various Trade Associations

Yesterday, various trade associations received a letter from the Bureau of Industry and Commerce of the Ministry of Industry, stating: "We have received instructions from the Ministry of Industry, based on the resolution of the Industrial and Commercial Conference, regarding the industrial standards proposal, requesting that you properly stipulate the standards for raw materials and products in various industries and submit them to the Ministry for reference. Industrial standards are indeed an urgent matter for the country today. Chinese industry has traditionally been laissez-faire, without any standards. The same product has a diverse and inconsistent range of styles, and products of the same style vary in quality, with both perfections and flaws, leading to deception. As a result, buyers find it difficult to distinguish and disregard them, and manufacturers lament the difficulty of sales and the lack of business prosperity. Industrialized countries around the world have adopted certain standards for both raw materials and products. Chinese industry has always lagged behind, and if we do not make reasonable improvements, the future of industry is unthinkable. We hereby request your association to convene your industry peers to concretely discuss and stipulate simple standards for various items, such as quality, style, shape, width, and other aspects of products and raw materials, and send a reply to this bureau for verification and implementation, so that those seeking them can easily choose and promote consumption."

Customs Collects Special Tax on Factory Silk

▲ Non-Factory Silk is Generally Exempted

The General Affairs Office of the Jianghai Customs issued a public notice stating: "We have received an order from the Inspector General of Customs forwarding an order from the Customs Administration of the Ministry of Finance stating that a special tax of 30 yuan in national currency per picul should be levied on yellow and white silk transported from Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces to foreign countries, as previously announced by this customs. This special tax is approved to be collected on factory silk transported to foreign countries, and all other non-factory silk is generally exempted. We hereby notify all merchants to be aware of this."

Municipal Chamber of Commerce Requests Refund of Stamp Tax Fine

▲ Fine for Unstamped Invoices Ten Years Ago

The Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce, regarding the stamp tax bureau's fine for unstamped invoices from ten years ago, sent a special letter to the Jiangsu Provincial Stamp Tax Bureau the day before yesterday requesting a full refund of the fine. The original letter stated: "Rice shops have complained that Suilong and other rice shops have been fined by the stamp tax bureau for unstamped invoices from ten years ago. This association, after inquiring with your bureau, determined the annual inspection and punishment period. Subsequently, on the 3rd of this month, we approved your bureau's reply that the inspection would be held in the first half of this year, and the invoices and receipts used by the merchants would be limited. Any unstamped items found after January 1st of the 19th year should be detained and reported, and those before January 1st of the 19th year should be exempted. The rice shops claimed that the fines were all for old invoices, some dating back more than ten years, which sounds absurd. If they cannot provide factual evidence, it would be close to sensationalism. Even if the inspectors made a mistake, the case was reviewed, how could such an error occur? After forwarding this to the public association, we received a reply from the rice shop industry association on the 13th of this month, stating that the Shangbao Stamp Tax Bureau's reply stated that all cases to be fined are reviewed on a case-by-case basis, demonstrating the bureau's meticulousness. However, even the most careful can make mistakes. The association's previous claim that fines were levied on waste invoices from more than ten years ago is indeed based on facts and is not a fabrication. According to a letter from member Dexing Rice Shop, they were summoned and fined by the Public Security Bureau of the Second District, First Branch, for unstamped invoices from the Gengshen and Xinyou years. These waste invoices date back more than ten years and were fined 10 yuan. The Gengshen and Xinyou years' invoices were sent to the association for transfer and negotiation. The Gengshen and Xinyou years are indeed more than ten years ago. If there was no concrete evidence, the association would not have dared to make such an inquiry. We are now sending the original letter and the two Gengshen and Xinyou invoices and fine notice for your review. Please inform the bureau of the reason for the error in fining invoices from more than ten years ago, causing the association's members to suffer unnecessary losses. Please return the wrongly fined money in full to alleviate the merchants' difficulties. Attached is a letter from the association with one invoice each from the Gengshen and Xinyou years and one fine notice. This fine notice was issued on May 20th of this year, and the unstamped invoices being fined are one from the Gengshen year and one from the Xinyou year. According to your bureau's reply, they occurred many years ago and are not subject to detention and fine. We are sending two invoices, the original fine notice, and the original letter for your review. Please approve the registration of the wrongly fined case and return the 10 yuan fine in full to comply with the limited detention and fine measures. We sincerely hope for your cooperation."

Epidemic in the City Worsens

Recently, due to the sultry and erratic weather, the epidemic has also become unpredictable. The number of patients at the Chinese Red Cross Society's Epidemic Hospital has suddenly increased, and the types of illnesses have also diversified. The day before yesterday, Zhang Suozi, the three-year-old son of Zhang Xibin, who resided at 22 Deming Lane, East Pushi Road, suddenly contracted pneumonia with a fever of over 104 degrees. He was sent to the hospital, where the attending director Dr. Wang Zhenchuan administered injections and other treatments, staying up all night. He only recovered yesterday evening. In addition, there are many cases of malaria, dysentery, and measles. Investigations show that the origin of these epidemics is mostly due to the infectious onset of food poisoning, which can be life-threatening in the shortest period of time. They should be sent to the hospital for diagnosis and treatment as soon as possible. Methods such as pinching and scraping are most likely to cause delays. Citizens must pay attention.

Fire Insurance Pays Compensation with 10% Penalty

The Zhenhua Grocery Store at No. 30 Jixiang Street, French Concession, caught fire and spread on the 10th of this month. The Fire Brigade rushed to extinguish the fire. The police station investigated and found that the store had fire insurance of 7,000 taels of silver. Therefore, they summoned the store to the French Court yesterday for questioning. First, the police chief reported the situation, and Chen Kangnian, the store manager, stated that it was indeed caused by a short circuit upstairs. The Chinese and Western judges ordered the defendant to pay compensation with a 10% penalty as a warning.

Tan Yunsan Donates Calligraphy to Relieve Guangdong Disaster

Lingnan calligrapher Tan Yunsan, in view of the flooding in Guangdong Province, the material losses of which amount to tens of millions, and the 100,000 compatriots who are in danger and have nowhere to turn, and if they are not rescued quickly, 100,000 disaster victims will inevitably become starving corpses, has developed a compassionate heart and donated a thousand pieces of calligraphy, including couplets, hall hangings, plaques, signboards, folding fans, and calling cards. He will not charge for his calligraphy skills. For each piece, regardless of size, a fee of one yuan in silver will be collected in Shanghai, and one and a half yuan in foreign areas. If you entrust the purchase of calligraphy, an additional half yuan will be charged. The funds raised from the calligraphy, after deducting 30% for the collection point and ink grinding fees, will be used to relieve the disaster. All people from all walks of life at home and abroad who wish to contribute to charity and obtain Tan Yunsan's calligraphy can submit their requests to Mr. Peng Yuzhi at the Taotao Restaurant on Dong Wuchang Road, North Sichuan Road, Shanghai, or to the Xiyin Study upstairs at 246 Xin Guangdong Street, Zhabei.

▲ Xishan: More than 400 Xishan natives in Shanghai, including Xu Mingli, believe that the temporary executive committee of the Jinting Assembly Hall's plan to renovate the city houses outside the hall will result in a great loss of rights. They have been convening meetings of the fellow villagers association for days to discuss remedies. On one hand, they have hired a lawyer to publish a warning in the newspaper to the temporary executive committee of the assembly hall. They have also submitted a petition to the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau and convened a general meeting of fellow villagers for public discussion. The temporary executive committee of the Jinting Assembly Hall published a statement in the newspaper that was full of contradictions. The Xishan natives were furious after reading it and issued a collective rebuttal. The rebuttal roughly stated: "After reading the announcement of the temporary executive committee of the Jinting Assembly Hall, we can only laugh it off. The language is contradictory and the explanation is not coherent. The committee drafted a seven-year advance payment construction plan and distributed it to fellow villagers. Since the majority of fellow villagers responded with approval, why not implement it immediately? Instead, you are separately recruiting tenants for lease, without notifying fellow villagers again, and hurriedly signing contracts for lease and construction. Are you not trying to hide the truth from the eyes and ears of our fellow villagers? Moreover, the monthly rent is only 180 taels, which is intended to be used for accumulating grain funds, school subsidies, and the assembly hall's operating expenses. Even a clever woman would find this difficult. As for not requiring land certificate guarantees, why did the land certificate custodian, Sen Ji Yi, and others, publish an announcement stating that they would only be responsible for safekeeping until the end of July? If we do not oppose it soon, the sovereignty will be lost. In short, this is public property and must be agreed upon by the public. We will never allow it to be manipulated by a few people."
